<code_state>

<file>
skill/recall.md

**Summary:**
Layered search protocol for `/doc-harness recall [query]`. Read-only. Token-efficient.

**Key elements:**
- 4 query types: A (status/plan), B (history/decision), C (file lookup), D (synthesis)
- 5 search layers (0→4): CLAUDE.md → CURRENT_STATUS → WORKLOG → FILE_INDEX → individual files
- **Token-efficiency rules (normative)**:
  - Phase 2 "Zero Token Layer": check if answer already exists in context (Recovery Chain already read, recent files, conversation history)
  - FILE_INDEX: grep only, never read full file
  - WORKLOG: read TOC (first 20 lines) + grep matching phases only
  - Sub-indexes: grep-recurse only
  - Individual files: grep `-C 3` for keywords; files >100 lines — prohibit full read
  - >10 matches: show top 5, ask user which to deep-read
- Stop early: don't read Layer 4 if Layers 0–2 answer the query
- Cite every claim: `(CURRENT_STATUS.md §Car Body)`, `(notes/design.md#L42)`, etc.
- Output format: header with query/type/layers-searched → Layer excerpts → Synthesis → Not Found

**Latest version:**
~230 lines; token-efficiency rules in §Search Rules (Normative), Layer 3/4 search strategies.
</file>

<file>
PHILOSOPHY.md

**Summary:**
Universal principles forged by project practice. Created 2026-04-22.

**Key elements:**
- Principle 1: **深入浅出** — Perspective-switching methodology. Systems can be examined at detail or at distance. When stuck, force a zoom-out to verify the problem still exists and test methods are valid.
- Principle 2: **知识的诅咒** — Curse of knowledge. Agents (human and AI) assume others know what they know. Always provide full background; never assume shared context.
- Each entry: principle statement, practice that forged it, scope of applicability, first-recorded date.
- User standard: principles must be universal ("放之四海而皆准"), not tied to specific technical events.

**Latest version:**
37 lines (concise).
</file>

    16	
    17	## 为什么会有这件事
    18

    20	
    21	1. 不同项目的 agent 不共享会话上下文
    22	2. 聊天中口述的需求/承诺会在会话结束时丢失
    23	3. 跨项目的需求/交付/确认如果不以文件形式落盘，就无法被对方 agent 下次会话的 Recovery Chain 拾取
    24

<system>236 lines read from file starting from line 1. Total lines in file: 236. End of file reached.</system>
     1	---

     6	status: actioned

     8	priority: high
     9	---
    10	
    11	# WhoAMI → doc-harness：四项改进建议
    12	
    13	## 零、目的
    14	
    15	doc-harness 是 portfolio 下几乎所有项目的基础架构骨架。过去一段时间在 WhoAMI、SMSS、lit-system-api 等项目里密集使用之后，发现**几类反复出现的问题**。本信提出四项建议，希望 doc-harness 的下一版 skill 定义能把它们吸纳进去。
    16	
    17	此外，附带转发一封 SMSS 之前发的"跨项目通信机制"推广信——**inbox/outbox 机制应该成为 doc-harness 标配的一部分**，而不是各项目各自摸索。
    18	
    19	---
    20	
    21	## 一、建议 1：Recovery Chain 的两层结构 + self-contained 约束
    22	
    23	### 当前缺口
    24	
    25	现行 doc-harness 规范对 Recovery Chain 的描述比较简略（典型写法"读 CLAUDE.md → CURRENT_STATUS → FILE_INDEX"）。实际使用中会反复出现三个症状：
    26	
    27	**症状 A：新 agent 读了基础文档，但缺少"当前要做什么"的操作性知识**
    28	比如 WhoAMI 项目，新 agent 读完 CLAUDE/CURRENT_STATUS 后，仍然不知道：
    29	- 生产服务器怎么部署（凭证在哪？脚本怎么跑？）
    30	- 正在等哪个外部项目交付什么（下周一 lit-system-api 要 ship cite marker，需要等）
    31	- 要改 LLM preset 时用哪个（用户明确不要 Claude 额度紧张）
    32	
    33	这些是"活的"操作性知识，会随工作推进变化。FILE_INDEX 有它们但 FILE_INDEX 是索引不是指令——新 agent 不会主动翻索引除非明确被指向。
    34	
    35	**症状 B："always read inbox"作为默认基线不合理**
    36	如果 inbox 积累了 10000 封旧信，全读一遍既浪费 context 又无意义。只有 `status: unread` 才是必须处理的。
    37	
    38	**症状 C：agent-side 特性（Claude 的 memory 系统）被绑进项目文档**
    39	在修正 Recovery Chain 过程中，WhoAMI 的 agent 一开始把 memory 文件链接放进 CLAUDE.md 的 Recovery Chain 里。这违反了项目文档应当自含的基本原则——memory 是 Claude 独有特性，不能成为 doc-harness 架构的依赖。换用其他 agent 或未来 Claude 功能变化时，这些链接会失效。
    40	
    41	### 建议的规范
    42	
    43	在 doc-harness skill 定义中，把 Recovery Chain 写成**两层结构** + **一条硬约束**：
    44	
    45	```markdown
    46	## Recovery Chain
    47	
    48	### 必读（Must-read — essential baseline for any continuation）
    49	
    50	1. This file (CLAUDE.md)
    51	2. CURRENT_STATUS.md
    52	
    53	（基线应当精简，通常 2-3 条，不超过 4 条）
    54	
    55	### 条件读（Task-conditional — read only if the work matches）
    56	
    57	- If X1: read Y1
    58	- If X2: read Y2
    59	- ... (5-10 条，随项目演化增减)
    60	
    61	### 元规则
    62	
    63	Recovery Chain 是活的：有新的工作类别出现时加条件读条目；旧类别退役时删除。
    64	Recovery Chain 必须 self-contained：所有引用指向项目内（或稳定路径的兄弟项目）的文件。
    65	不依赖 agent-side 特性（memory / 历史会话 / 外部服务）——那些可能在未来不存在。
    66	```
    67	
    68	**inbox 的正确归类**：放在"条件读"里，写作 "If `inbox/` has any `status: unread` messages, read them"。不进入必读基线。
    69	
    70	### 这条建议的价值
    71	
    72	- 新 agent 每次冷启动的 context 成本下降
    73	- 活的操作知识（部署脚本、等待的交付、preset 选择）有固定的"注册入口"
    74	- doc-harness 不被绑定到任何特定 agent 生态
    75	
    76	### 来源
    77	
    78	2026-04-18 WhoAMI 和 SMSS 的 agent 分别遇到这个问题，经和用户三轮讨论后定型。WhoAMI 的 `CLAUDE.md` 已经按这个结构改造，可作参考实现。
    79	
    80	---
    81	
    82	## 二、建议 2：WORKLOG 长度监控 + 归档
    83	
    84	### 现象
    85	
    86	WORKLOG 是 append-only 的历史档案。长期使用下**必然不断增长**。WhoAMI 的 WORKLOG 目前已有 8 个 Phase、接近 1500 行。SMSS 的 WORKLOG 更大。
    87	
    88	问题不是"WORKLOG 大"本身（它就是档案，应该完整），而是：
    89	
    90	- **新 agent 的 Recovery Chain 条件读里可能指向 WORKLOG**，但它已经大到不适合从头读
    91	- **WORKLOG 里近期 Phase 对当前工作重要，远期 Phase 对当前工作几乎无关**
    92	- **FILE_INDEX 只登记 "WORKLOG.md"，没有区分"当前版"和"归档版"**
    93	
    94	### 建议
    95	
    96	doc-harness 在 "Session End Checklist" 里加一项：**check WORKLOG.md length; archive when exceeds threshold**。
    97	
    98	具体做法：
    99	
   100	- **阈值**：比如 WORKLOG 超过 2000 行 或 超过 20 个 Phase 时触发
   101	- **归档动作**：保留最近 N 个 Phase（比如最近 3 个）在 `WORKLOG.md`，把更早的剪切到 `WORKLOG_ARCHIVE_<yyyy-mm>.md`
   102	- **归档文件在 FILE_INDEX 单独列出**，并在 `WORKLOG.md` 开头加一行指针："Earlier history in `WORKLOG_ARCHIVE_2025-Q4.md`, `WORKLOG_ARCHIVE_2026-Q1.md`, etc."
   103	- **归档触发方式**：session end checklist 自检时提示 agent，由 agent 执行（或至少提醒用户确认）
   104	
   105	### 用户原话（2026-04-19）
   106	
   107	> "Doc-harness 应该检查 worklog 的长度，太长了的时候应该存档备查，保持一个当前工作的版本即可。"
   108	
   109	---
   110	
   111	## 三、建议 3：长期知识载体（Vision / Parking Lot / Philosophy）
   112	
   113	### 当前缺口
   114	
   115	doc-harness 目前的四文档体系（CLAUDE / CURRENT_STATUS / FILE_INDEX / WORKLOG）很适合**中短期工作流**：
   116	
   117	- CURRENT_STATUS 记"当前阶段"
   118	- WORKLOG 记"历史做了什么"
   119	
   120	但有几类信息**不合适放在这四份里**：
   121	
   122	**A. 长期愿景（Long-term vision）**
   123	"这个项目终极要变成什么样"——当前不做但不能忘记。放 CURRENT_STATUS 会过时，放 WORKLOG 会埋没在细节里。
   124	
   125	**B. 想做但暂时做不了的事（Parking lot）**
   126	"这个优化应该做，但需要某个前置条件；前置条件可能几个月后才具备"——当前不做但不能让它被新工作覆盖后遗忘。
   127	
   128	**C. 哲学 / 从实践中提炼的原则（Philosophy）**
   129	"我们发现 X 原则在多个项目里反复被验证"——跨越具体项目的工作道理、经验、教训。不属于任何一个项目。
   130	
   131	### 建议
   132	
   133	在 doc-harness 四文档之外引入**可选的三份文档**，各项目按需创建：
   134	
   135	1. **`VISION.md`**（Long-term vision）
   136	   - 项目终极形态描述
   137	   - 大跨度里程碑（不同于 headlights 的近期 next-steps）
   138	   - 一般稳定，半年级别更新一次
   139	
   140	2. **`PARKING_LOT.md`**（Deferred items）
   141	   - 想做但现在做不了的具体事项
   142	   - 每项标注：为什么推迟 / 前置条件 / 何时检查是否可以开始
   143	   - 新工作覆盖旧关注时，把旧关注从 CURRENT_STATUS 移到这里而不是丢掉
   144	
   145	3. **`PHILOSOPHY.md`**（或 portfolio 级的 `PRINCIPLES.md`）
   146	   - 项目无关的经验 / 原则 / 教训
   147	   - "Recovery Chain 必须 self-contained" 就是这类
   148	   - "本地=生产预演" 就是这类
   149	   - 这些原则会反哺 doc-harness skill 本身的演化
   150	
   151	### 与 Recovery Chain 的接口
   152	
   153	这三份都加入条件读分支：
   154	
   155	```
   156	- 决策跨度半年以上的事 / 验证项目定位 → VISION.md
   157	- 规划新工作时检查是否与长期目标冲突 → PARKING_LOT.md（看有什么老债等着复活）
   158	- 设计重大决策 → PHILOSOPHY.md
   159	```
   160	
   161	### 用户原话（2026-04-19）
   162	
   163	> "Doc-harness 应该有能力记录'长期的事情'。比如长期的愿景，计划做、但暂时做不了、又怕将来忘记（随着工作的推进埋没到 worklog 中）的事情。甚至应该有'哲学'文档，记录那些从实践中带来的不局限于具体项目工作的道理、经验、教训等等。"
   164	
   165	---
   166	
   167	## 四、建议 4：inbox/outbox 跨项目通信机制应成为 doc-harness 标配
   168	
   169	### 背景
   170	
   171	SMSS 项目的 agent 在 2026-04-18 主动向 portfolio 所有项目发了一封强制执行信（附在本信 inbox，建议先读），要求每个项目在 CLAUDE.md 里加入 inbox/outbox 协议 iron rule。
   172	
   173	协议权威文档：`D:\Projects\docs\INTERPROJECT_COMM_SPEC.md`
   174	
   175	机制简述：
   176	- 每个项目有 `inbox/` 和 `outbox/` 目录
   177	- 消息是 YAML frontmatter + Markdown body 的 `.md` 文件
   178	- 命名：`YYYY-MM-DD-from-[source]-[topic].md`
   179	- 生命周期：unread → read → actioned，append-only，需回复就写新消息
   180	
   181	### 当前问题
   182	
   183	- 机制已经在 WhoAMI / SMSS / lit-system-api / 文献系统等多项目间实战跑起来（日当下 10+ 封），效果很好
   184	- 但每个项目 agent 是**临时被告知**这个机制的，不是 doc-harness 一开始就强制建立
   185	- **doc-harness 自己也没装这个机制**——这就是为什么这封信要先帮 doc-harness 创建 inbox/outbox
   186	
   187	### 建议
   188	
   189	doc-harness skill 在初始化一个新项目时，**默认创建**：
   190	- `inbox/`（空目录 + `.gitkeep` 或 README）
   191	- `outbox/`（同上）
   192	- CLAUDE.md 的 iron rules 区自动包含"项目间通讯走 inbox/outbox"的完整条目
   193	- Recovery Chain 的条件读里自动包含"If `inbox/` has any `status: unread` messages"
   194	
   195	这样每个用 doc-harness 初始化的新项目**天生就支持跨项目通信**，不需要事后补。
   196	
   197	### 权威规范已经写好
   198	
   199	`D:\Projects\docs\INTERPROJECT_COMM_SPEC.md` 第 §98-117 行已有 "Required Iron Rule for Participating Projects" 节，里面是可直接复制的模板。doc-harness skill 只需引用或镶嵌这段即可。
   200	
   201	---
   202	
   203	## 五、实施建议（优先级）
   204	
   205	| 项 | 优先级 | 工作量 | 影响 |
   206	|---|---|---|---|
   207	| 1. Recovery Chain 两层结构 + self-contained | 🔴 P0 | 中（改 skill 定义 + 现有项目批量迁移） | 所有项目受益 |
   208	| 4. inbox/outbox 成为标配 | 🔴 P0 | 小（skill 模板加几行） | 跨项目协作健壮性 |
   209	| 2. WORKLOG 归档机制 | 🟡 P1 | 小（session end checklist 加一条） | 防长文档腐烂 |
   210	| 3. VISION / PARKING_LOT / PHILOSOPHY 可选文档 | 🟢 P2 | 中（规范 + 模板） | 长期知识保留 |
   211	
   212	建议 1 和 4 可以一起做（都是 skill 模板调整）；2 是机械规则；3 需要先定义清楚三份文档的边界。
   213	
   214	---
   215	
   216	## 六、参考实现
   217	
   218	- **WhoAMI 的新版 Recovery Chain**：`D:/Projects/WhoAMI/CLAUDE.md`（2026-04-19 已按建议 1 改造完成，可作参考）
   219	- **portfolio inbox/outbox 规范**：`D:/Projects/docs/INTERPROJECT_COMM_SPEC.md`
   220	- **WhoAMI 的 Operations Cheatsheet**（操作性知识如何组织的示例）：`D:/Projects/WhoAMI/CURRENT_STATUS.md` 末尾
   221	
   222	---

   229

    47	
    48	## 三、根因分析（多层）
    49	
    50	### 3.1 直接原因：项目身份认知错误
    51	
    52	Agent 在调查过程中，大量阅读了 lit-system-api 的代码（`app/agent.py`、`app/diagnostics.py` 等），导致认知逐渐漂移——把自己当成了 lit-system-api 的维护者，而非 WhoAMI 的代理。
    53	
    54	### 3.2 触发因素：跨项目深度调研
    55	
    56	本次调查需要理解 lit-system-api 的内部机制（`_extract_vault_ids_for_map`、`_classify_llm_error`、上游重试逻辑、F-A1 诊断系统等），Agent 在 lit-system-api 代码库中花费了过多时间，而 WhoAMI 的入口文档（CLAUDE.md）没有强制的身份锚定。
    57	
    58	### 3.3 深层原因：Recovery Chain 缺乏身份校验
    59	
    60	WhoAMI 的 Recovery Chain 第一步是读 `CLAUDE.md`，但 `CLAUDE.md` 中没有任何关于"你是哪个项目的代理"的声明。Agent 在 context compaction 后恢复工作时，如果 lit-system-api 的文件在上下文中占主导，很容易产生身份混淆。
    61	
    62	### 3.4 机制缺陷：doc-harness 未规范身份锚定
    63	
    64	doc-harness 规范（`DOC_HARNESS_SPEC.md`）规定了 Recovery Chain、CURRENT_STATUS、FILE_INDEX 等结构，但**没有要求每个项目的 CLAUDE.md 必须包含 agent 身份声明**。这是一个规范缺口。
    65	
    66	---
    67

   117	
   118	## 六、教训
   119	
   120	### 6.1 对 Agent
   121	
   122	1. **跨项目调研是危险操作** — 深度阅读其他项目的代码会潜移默化地改变自我认知。必须在调研前后显式确认自己的身份。
   123	2. **outbox/ 不是共享目录** — 每个项目的 outbox 只属于该项目。向其他项目发信时，必须写入自己的 outbox + 复制到对方的 inbox。
   124	3. **内部文档是红线** — 永远不要修改其他项目的 CURRENT_STATUS.md、FILE_INDEX.md、WORKLOG.md。这些文件是对方 agent 的"大脑"，修改它们等于篡改对方的记忆。
   125	4. **from 字段是法律责任** — from 字段声明了信件的发出方。写错 from 字段会导致对方 agent 无法正确路由回复，甚至引发安全审计问题。
   126	
   127	### 6.2 对 doc-harness 规范
   128	
   129	1. **身份锚定应该是强制要求** — 每个项目的 CLAUDE.md 必须在最顶部包含不可忽略的身份声明。
   130	2. **跨项目操作应该有 checklist** — 当 agent 需要向其他项目发信或部署其他项目的代码时，应该有一个标准 checklist 来防止越界。
   131	3. **Recovery Chain 应该包含身份校验步骤** — 在"读 CLAUDE.md"之后，应该有一个显式步骤确认"我是 X 项目的代理"。
   132	
   133	---
   134	
   135	## 七、复现条件
   136	
   137	以下条件下可能再次发生类似事件：
   138	
   139	1. Agent 需要深度调研另一个项目的代码（>30 分钟阅读）
   140	2. Context compaction 后恢复工作，前一个项目的文件仍在上下文中
   141	3. 多个项目的 CLAUDE.md 同时在上下文中（如用户同时打开两个项目的文件）
   142	4. Agent 从其他项目的 inbox/outbox 中读取消息（只读操作也可能导致认知漂移）
   143	
   144	---
   145	
   146	## 八、检测指标
   147	
   148	如果出现以下行为，说明 Agent 可能正在经历身份混乱：
   149	
   150	- [ ] 向其他项目的 outbox/ 写入文件
   151	- [ ] 修改其他项目的内部文档（CURRENT_STATUS、FILE_INDEX、WORKLOG）
   152	- [ ] 发信时 from 字段写错了项目名
   153	- [ ] 发信时没有同时复制到对方的 inbox/
   154	- [ ] 在解释自己的行为时，用"我们"指代其他项目
   155

<!-- call_id: tool_kXaCI0Q8MPlED4grBKfEsHW3 -->
<system>182 lines read from file starting from line 1. Total lines in file: 182. End of file reached.</system>
     1	---
     2	from: whoami
     3	to: doc-harness
     4	date: 2026-04-22
     5	subject: 【经验分享】Windows 环境下 GitHub push 失败的完整解决路径
     6	status: actioned
     7	priority: normal
     8	---
     9	
    10	# WhoAMI → doc-harness：GitHub push 实战经验报告
    11	
    12	## 背景
    13	
    14	WhoAMI 项目（Windows 本地开发环境）在尝试向 GitHub 推送时频繁遭遇 SSL/TLS 握手失败。经过向 lit-system-api 请教 + 本地反复验证，最终找到稳定方案。现将完整经验归档，供 doc-harness 项目参考。
    15	
    16	---
    17	
    18	## 一、问题现象
    19	
    20	### 错误信息 A
    21	```
    22	fatal: unable to access 'https://github.com/cilidinezy-commits/whoami.git/':
    23	schannel: failed to receive handshake, SSL/TLS connection failed
    24	```
    25	
    26	### 错误信息 B
    27	```
    28	Failure when receiving data from the peer
    29	```
    30	
    31	### 环境信息
    32	- 操作系统：Windows 11
    33	- Git 协议：HTTPS
    34	- 网络：家用宽带，无企业防火墙
    35	- 代理工具：Clash Verge（已运行，端口 7897）
    36	
    37	---
    38	
    39	## 二、诊断过程
    40	
    41	### Step 1：确认问题范围
    42	
    43	| 测试 | 结果 | 结论 |
    44	|------|------|------|
    45	| `curl -I https://github.com` | HTTP 000 / 403 | 本地→GitHub 直连 HTTPS 不稳定 |
    46	| 服务器 paramiko SSH 操作 | 正常 | 服务器网络无问题 |
    47	| `git push` 同一仓库 | 失败 | 问题在本地 Git → GitHub 链路 |
    48	
    49	**结论**：不是仓库权限问题，不是 GitHub 服务问题，是本地网络到 GitHub CDN 的链路不稳定。
    50	
    51	### Step 2：尝试单一配置
    52	
    53	| 配置项 | 值 | 结果 |
    54	|--------|-----|------|
    55	| `http.sslBackend = schannel` | 仅此项 | 仍失败（`Failure when receiving data from the peer`）|
    56	| `http.proxy = http://127.0.0.1:7897` | 仅此项 | 仍失败（SSL 握手阶段即断）|
    57	
    58	**结论**：单一配置不足以解决问题，需要组合使用。
    59	
    60	### Step 3：组合配置验证
    61	
    62	以下四项配置**同时生效**后，push 立即成功：
    63	
    64	```bash
    65	git config --global http.sslBackend schannel
    66	git config --global http.proxy http://127.0.0.1:7897
    67	git config --global https.proxy http://127.0.0.1:7897
    68	git config --global http.lowSpeedLimit 1000
    69	git config --global http.lowSpeedTime 60
    70	```
    71	
    72	---
    73	
    74	## 三、最终生效配置详解
    75	
    76	### 1. `http.sslBackend = schannel`
    77	
    78	- **作用**：让 Git 使用 Windows 原生的 SSL/TLS 库（schannel），而非 OpenSSL
    79	- **原因**：Windows 环境下 schannel 对系统证书的兼容性更好
    80	- **注意**：单独使用不够，必须配合代理
    81	
    82	### 2. `http.proxy` + `https.proxy = http://127.0.0.1:7897`
    83	
    84	- **作用**：所有 Git HTTP/HTTPS 请求走本地代理（Clash Verge）
    85	- **关键发现**：这是**决定性配置**。本地直连 GitHub 的 HTTPS 链路在握手阶段即被中断，走代理后链路稳定
    86	- **代理端口**：取决于你的代理工具（Clash 默认 7890 或 7897，v2rayN 默认 10809，请根据实际情况调整）
    87	
    88	### 3. `http.lowSpeedLimit = 1000` + `http.lowSpeedTime = 60`
    89	
    90	- **作用**：如果 60 秒内下载速度低于 1000 bytes/s，Git 自动重试
    91	- **原因**：防止连接建立后、数据传输中途因网络抖动而静默失败
    92	
    93	---
    94	
    95	## 四、一键配置脚本
    96	
    97	```bash
    98	# Windows PowerShell / Git Bash
    99	
   100	git config --global http.sslBackend schannel
   101	
   102	# 根据你的代理工具调整端口
   103	# Clash Verge: 7897
   104	# Clash for Windows: 7890
   105	# v2rayN: 10809
   106	$PROXY_PORT = 7897
   107	
   108	git config --global http.proxy "http://127.0.0.1:$PROXY_PORT"
   109	git config --global https.proxy "http://127.0.0.1:$PROXY_PORT"
   110	git config --global http.lowSpeedLimit 1000
   111	git config --global http.lowSpeedTime 60
   112	
   113	# 验证配置
   114	git config --global --list | findstr "http\."
   115	```
   116	
   117	---
   118	
   119	## 五、验证方法
   120	
   121	```bash
   122	# 1. 查看当前配置
   123	git config --global --list | findstr "http\."
   124	
   125	# 2. 测试连接（不实际 push）
   126	git ls-remote https://github.com/cilidinezy-commits/whoami.git
   127	
   128	# 3. 小文件推送测试
   129	echo "test" >> test-push.txt
   130	git add test-push.txt
   131	git commit -m "test: verify push path"
   132	git push origin main
   133	
   134	# 4. 成功后删除测试文件
   135	git rm test-push.txt
   136	git commit -m "chore: remove push test file"
   137	git push origin main
   138	```
   139	
   140	---
   141	
   142	## 六、故障排除速查表
   143	
   144	| 现象 | 可能原因 | 解决 |
   145	|------|---------|------|
   146	| `schannel: failed to receive handshake` | SSL 后端不匹配 | `git config --global http.sslBackend schannel` |
   147	| `Failure when receiving data from the peer` | 网络链路中断 | 配置代理 + lowSpeedLimit |
   148	| `Could not resolve host` | DNS 问题 | 检查代理是否运行，或换 DNS |
   149	| `403 Forbidden` | 认证问题 | `git credential-manager reject ...` 后重新登录 |
   150	| Push 成功但极慢 | 带宽限制 | 确认代理正常运行，lowSpeedTime 适当调大 |
   151	
   152	---
   153	
   154	## 七、已知陷阱
   155	
   156	1. **PowerShell `>` 重定向产生 UTF-16 LE**：如果通过 `git show HEAD:file > file.txt` 提取文件，PowerShell 默认输出 UTF-16 LE（含 null bytes）。上传后会导致服务端 `SyntaxError`。解决方案：使用 Python `subprocess.run(..., capture_output=True)` + `open(..., 'wb')`。
   157	
   158	2. **代理端口会变**：Clash Verge 更新后端口可能从 7890 变为 7897，push 失败时首先检查代理端口是否正确。
   159	
   160	3. **全局配置影响所有仓库**：`git config --global` 会影响本地所有 Git 仓库。如只想影响单个仓库，去掉 `--global` 在仓库目录内执行。
   161	
   162	---
   163	
   164	## 八、WhoAMI 的推送现状
   165	
   166	配置生效后，WhoAMI 已成功推送以下 commits：
   167	
   168	```

   171	57dccc1  revert(front): do not filter '正在请求 AI 模型…' in frontend
   172	...
   173	```
   174	
   175	推送稳定，未再出现 SSL/TLS 握手失败。

    43	
    44	## Chapter 1: First Principles & Overview
    45	
    46	### 1.1 First Principle: "Write It Down or Lose It"
    47	
    48	All information in context is temporary. No matter how important an analysis result or how brilliant a design idea, if it is not **written to a file** and **registered in FILE_INDEX**, it effectively does not exist.
    49	
    50	- **Write it down**: Important information must be saved to a file. Not written = lost.
    51	- **Register it**: The file must be registered in FILE_INDEX. Not registered = exists but undiscoverable = effectively lost.
    52	
    53	This principle takes priority over all efficiency considerations. Better to create one extra file than to let information exist only in context.
    54	
    55	### 1.2 What is Doc Harness
    56	
    57	Doc Harness is an information management system composed of four core documents, serving a **project**. A project is the basic unit — a working paper, a software tool, a research initiative.
    58	
    59	| Document | Role | Core Responsibility | Update Frequency |
    60	|----------|------|-------------------|-----------------|
    61	| **CLAUDE.md** | Front door | Project entry, recovery chain, iron rules | Phase transitions |
    62	| **CURRENT_STATUS.md** | Moving car | Active phase info, recent history, next steps, phase principles | Every session |
    63	| **FILE_INDEX.md** | Library catalog | Index all project files by category | When files change |
    64	| **WORKLOG.md** | Dash cam | Permanently store complete work details from all phases | Phase transitions (batch) |
    65	
    66	### 1.3 Core Scenarios
    67	
    68	| Scenario | Need |
    69	|----------|------|
    70	| **New agent arrives** | Read CLAUDE.md → CURRENT_STATUS → know what to do |
    71	| **Context compact recovery** | Read CURRENT_STATUS → resume from car body |
    72	| **Cross-project switch** | Read target project's CLAUDE.md → quick orientation |
    73	| **During work** | Update CURRENT_STATUS car body + register new files in FILE_INDEX |
    74	
    75	### 1.4 No External Memory Dependency
    76	
    77	Doc Harness is fully self-contained. It does not depend on MEMORY.md, conversation history, or any agent's private memory. Any agent can fully recover project state by reading files alone.
    78	
    79	If the environment provides a memory system (e.g., Claude Code's MEMORY.md), it can serve as **supplementary acceleration** but is never a requirement for recovery.
    80	
    81	---
    82	
    83	## Chapter 2: CLAUDE.md — Entry Document
    84	
    85	### 2.1 Responsibilities
    86	- Tell newcomers "what this project is"
    87	- Provide recovery chain (reading order)
    88	- Define project-level iron rules (permanent, phase-independent)
    89	- Point to the other three core documents
    90	- Provide stable project-specific technical information
    91	
    92	### 2.2 What it does NOT do
    93	- Does not record detailed current state (→ CURRENT_STATUS)
    94	- Does not list all files (→ FILE_INDEX)
    95	- Does not record historical work details (→ WORKLOG)
    96	
    97	### 2.3 Template
    98	
    99	CLAUDE.md consists of three parts: project-specific information + embedded operational rules + pointer to full spec.
   100	
   101	```markdown
   102	# [PROJECT_NAME] — Entry Document
   103	
   104	**Last updated**: YYYY-MM-DD
   105	**Current phase**: [Phase name] (⏳/⏸️/✅)
   106	**One-line status (as of YYYY-MM-DD)**: [Brief description]
   107	
   108	---
   109	
   110	## Recovery Chain
   111	
   112	Recovery Chain is the entry ritual for any agent or human resuming work on this project.
   113	It has two layers.
   114	
   115	### Must-read (baseline)
   116	
   117	Files any continuation must read. Keep to 2–3 entries.
   118	
   119	1. This file (CLAUDE.md)
   120	2. `CURRENT_STATUS.md`
   121	
   122	### Task-conditional
   123	
   124	Read only if the work matches. Grows and shrinks as the project evolves.
   125	
   126	- If looking up a specific file: read `FILE_INDEX.md`
   127	- If investigating historical phase details: read `WORKLOG.md`
   128	- [Add project-specific entries as needed — e.g., "If doing X: read Y.md"]
   129	
   130	### Meta-rules
   131	
   132	- Recovery Chain is **self-contained**: every entry points to a file inside the project
   133	  (or a stable sibling-project path). Do not depend on agent-side features
   134	  (memory systems, chat history, external services) — those may not exist for the next agent.
   135	- Recovery Chain is **living**: add entries when new classes of work appear; remove entries
   136	  when work categories retire. Review at phase transitions.
   137	
   138	## Project Overview
   139	
   140	[3-5 lines: project goals, outputs, key context]
   141	
   142	## Project-Level Iron Rules
   143	
   144	[Permanently valid, phase-independent rules]
   145	- Iron rule 1: ...
   146	- Iron rule 2: ...
   147	
   148	## Key Technical Information
   149	
   150	[Stable technical details: build commands, path conventions, dependencies]
   151	
   152	## Sub-projects (if any)
   153	
   154	- `subproject/` → see [subproject/CLAUDE.md](subproject/CLAUDE.md) (status: ⏳/⏸️/✅)
   155	
   156	## Doc Harness — Operational Rules
   157	
   158	[EMBED FULL CONTENT OF operational_rules.md HERE (~106 lines).
   159	 These rules are the complete guide for daily status document maintenance.
   160	 For full design rationale, see DOC_HARNESS_SPEC.md in project root.]
   161	```
   162	
   163	The complete operational rules are in `operational_rules.md`. The `/doc-harness init` skill embeds the current version automatically when creating CLAUDE.md.
   164	
   165	### 2.4 Update Rules
   166	- Update "current phase" and body content at phase transitions
   167	- Refresh "one-line status (as of date)" at every session end
   168	- Update "iron rules" when new rules are added
   169	- Operational rules section generally not modified — determined by the spec version at creation time
   170	
   171	---
   172	
   173	## Chapter 3: CURRENT_STATUS.md — Active Status Document
   174	
   175	### 3.1 Role and Structure
   176	
   177	CURRENT_STATUS is the project's **active nerve center**. Think of the project as a car moving forward; CURRENT_STATUS is the cockpit view. Four sections, each with a distinct role, a distinct update rhythm, and a distinct metaphor:
   178	
   179	- **§1 Tire Tracks (Recent Completed)** — what you see in the rear-view mirror. The last 2–3 completed phases, each in 3–5 lines. Enough to situate "where have we been" without fetching the WORKLOG. Each entry points to the WORKLOG chapter for details. Rolling window: when a new phase completes, the oldest entry drops off.
   180	- **§2 Car Body (Current Work)** — the car itself, where you are right now. The full working record of the current phase: phase goal, each completed step (what was done, files created, key decisions), unresolved issues. This is the section you edit most — every meaningful step lands here. At phase transition its contents move into WORKLOG (permanent archive) and the body is cleared for the next phase.
   181	- **§3 Headlights (Next Steps)** — what the lights illuminate ahead. Immediate actions (1–3 concrete next steps) plus longer-range plans. When a session ends, the headlights should still point at something actionable so the next agent (or you) knows what to pick up. Updated every session.
   182	- **§4 Driving Manual (Working Principles)** — rules for driving *this* car on *this* road. Phase-specific guidelines (e.g., "validate on out-of-sample data this phase" / "run typecheck before every commit"). They live and die with the phase; at transition, each is reviewed (promote to iron rule, keep, or remove — see §6.2.2).
   183	
   184	Summarized:
   185	
   186	| Section | Metaphor | Content | Lifecycle |
   187	|---------|----------|---------|-----------|
   188	| §1 Recent Completed | Tire Tracks | Brief summaries of 2–3 most recent completed phases (3–5 lines each) | Rolling window |
   189	| §2 Current Work | Car Body | Full detailed record of current phase | Transfers to WORKLOG at phase end |
   190	| §3 Next Steps | Headlights | Immediate actions + future plans | Updated every session |
   191	| §4 Working Principles | Driving Manual | Guidelines for this phase | Lives and dies with the phase |
   192	
   193	**Why the metaphor matters**: each section answers a different question an agent asks on arrival — *where have we been?* (tire tracks), *where are we now?* (car body), *where next?* (headlights), *how do we drive here?* (driving manual). Keeping the four physically separate prevents them from blurring — a common failure mode when status documents devolve into narrative prose.
   194	
   195	### 3.2 Template
   196	
   197	```markdown
   198	# CURRENT_STATUS — [PROJECT_NAME]
   199	
   200	**Last updated**: YYYY-MM-DD
   201	**Current phase**: [Phase name]
   202	
   203	---
   204	
   205	## Recent Completed (Tire Tracks)
   206	
   207	(For new projects: "Project just started, no completed phases yet")
   208	
   209	### [Phase N-1 name] (YYYY-MM-DD ~ YYYY-MM-DD)
   210	[3-5 line summary]
   211	Detailed record in WORKLOG.md § [corresponding title].
   212	
   213	### [Phase N-2 name] (YYYY-MM-DD ~ YYYY-MM-DD)
   214	[3-5 line summary]
   215	Detailed record in WORKLOG.md § [corresponding title].
   216	
   217	---
   218	
   219	## Current Work (Car Body)
   220	
   221	### Phase Goal
   222	[What this phase aims to accomplish]
   223	
   224	### Completed Steps
   225	
   226	#### [Step 1 name] (YYYY-MM-DD)
   227	- What was done
   228	- Files created → registered in FILE_INDEX
   229	- Key findings/decisions
   230	
   231	#### [Step 2 name] (YYYY-MM-DD)
   232	- ...
   233	
   234	### Unresolved Issues
   235	- [Issue 1]
   236	
   237	---
   238	
   239	## Next Steps (Headlights)
   240	
   241	### Immediate Actions
   242	1. [Next specific step]
   243	
   244	### Future Plans
   245	- [Longer-term plans]
   246	
   247	---
   248	
   249	## Current Working Principles (Driving Manual)
   250	
   251	[Guidelines for this phase. On phase transition, review each:
   252	 (a) promote to iron rule? (b) keep? (c) remove?
   253	 Mark satisfied principles [DONE] but keep until phase ends.]
   254	- Principle 1: ...
   255	- Principle 2: ...
   256	```
   257	
   258	### 3.3 Car Body Update Granularity
   259	
   260	**Key rule: Prepare for compact.** Do not assume the current session will complete normally.
   261	
   262	- After completing each **meaningful step**, update the car body. "Meaningful" = if context is lost now, the next agent needs to know this step is done.
   263	- Organize by **steps** (not sessions). One session may complete multiple steps; one step may span multiple sessions.
   264	- **Car body length guideline**: Keep under ~200 lines. If exceeded, consider triggering a phase transition.
   265	
   266	### 3.4 Update Rules
   267	- Update at least once per session (completed steps + headlights + last updated date)
   268	- When creating new files, record "created xxx" in car body AND register in FILE_INDEX
   269	
   270	---
   271	
   272	## Chapter 4: FILE_INDEX.md — File Index Document
   273	
   274	### 4.1 Responsibility
   275	Index all project files by **category**. Answer "what files exist, what are they, where are they?"
   276	
   277	### 4.2 Organization Principles
   278	- Group by category (`##` headings), **not by time**
   279	- Categories are project-specific; add or reorganize freely
   280	- Each entry: file path + one-line description
   281	- File spans two categories → place in primary only; other category writes "→ see §[primary]"
   282	
   283	### 4.3 Recursive Sub-indexes
   284	
   285	When a category exceeds **10 files**, recommend creating a sub-FILE_INDEX.md in that folder. Over **20 files**, it is mandatory.
   286	
   287	Parent FILE_INDEX keeps one line for that category:
   288	```markdown
   289	- `notes/findings/` → see [`notes/findings/FILE_INDEX.md`](notes/findings/FILE_INDEX.md)
   290	  (Ch04/Ch05 research findings, 38 files, organized by chapter)
   291	```
   292	
   293	Sub-FILE_INDEX header references parent:
   294	```markdown
   295	# FILE_INDEX — [Category name]
   296	**Parent index**: [`../../FILE_INDEX.md`](../../FILE_INDEX.md)
   297	```
   298	
   299	Recursion depth limited to **2 levels** (parent → child → grandchild). Deeper nesting indicates overly complex structure; consider reorganizing folders.
   300	
   301	### 4.4 Bulk File Creation
   302	
   303	When a session creates many similar files (e.g., 20 analysis reports at once), no need to register individually:
   304	1. Register the **folder** in FILE_INDEX with file count and naming pattern
   305	2. If count >10, create sub-FILE_INDEX.md
   306	3. Record in CURRENT_STATUS car body: "Created N files in xxx/, naming pattern: ..."
   307	
   308	### 4.5 Template
   309	
   310	```markdown
   311	# FILE_INDEX — [PROJECT_NAME]
   312	
   313	**Last updated**: YYYY-MM-DD
   314	
   315	---
   316	
   317	## Core Documents
   318	- `CLAUDE.md` — Project entry
   319	- `CURRENT_STATUS.md` — Active status
   320	- `FILE_INDEX.md` — This file
   321	- `WORKLOG.md` — Work history
   322	
   323	## [Category 1]
   324	- `path/file1.md` — Description
   325	- `path/file2.md` — Description
   326	
   327	## [Category 2]
   328	- `path/folder/` → see [`path/folder/FILE_INDEX.md`] (N files, brief description)
   329	
   330	## [Category 3]
   331	- `path/file3.py` — Description
   332	```
   333	
   334	### 4.6 Update Rules
   335	- Register when creating new files
   336	- Remove when deleting/archiving files
   337	- No need to update every session — only when the file system changes
   338	
   339	---
   340	
   341	## Chapter 5: WORKLOG.md — Work Log Document
   342	
   343	### 5.1 Responsibility
   344	Permanently store **complete** work details from all phases. Content comes from CURRENT_STATUS during phase transitions.
   345	
   346	### 5.2 Table of Contents (TOC)
   347	
   348	WORKLOG maintains a TOC at the top for quick navigation in long documents:
   349	
   350	```markdown
   351	# WORKLOG — [PROJECT_NAME]
   352	
   353	## TOC
   354	| Phase | Time | Anchor |
   355	|-------|------|--------|
   356	| Phase 5: Format fixes | 2026-03-29~03-30 | [→](#phase-5-format-fixes) |
   357	| Phase 4: Literature | 2026-03-27~03-29 | [→](#phase-4-literature) |
   358	| Phase 3: Ch5 rebuild | 2026-03-25~03-27 | [→](#phase-3-ch5-rebuild) |
   359	
   360	---
   361	
   362	## Phase 5: Format fixes
   363	[Detailed content...]
   364	
   365	## Phase 4: Literature
   366	[Detailed content...]
   367	```
   368	
   369	### 5.3 Content Format
   370	
   371	Each phase is a top-level section (`##`):
   372	
   373	```markdown
   374	## Phase N: [Name] (YYYY-MM-DD ~ YYYY-MM-DD)
   375	
   376	### Phase Summary
   377	[3-5 line summary added at phase end]
   378	
   379	### Detailed Record
   380	[Content copied verbatim from CURRENT_STATUS car body]
   381	```
   382	
   383	### 5.4 Modification Rules
   384	
   385	- **Allowed**: Append summary or errata at the beginning of existing phases
   386	- **Allowed**: Add new entries to the TOC
   387	- **Forbidden**: Modify or delete content copied from CURRENT_STATUS
   388	- Factual errors: annotate as `[Erratum (YYYY-MM-DD): actual value was 4087, not 4090]`
   389	
   390	### 5.5 Archival
   391	
   392	WORKLOG is append-only, so it inevitably grows. A 2000-line WORKLOG is a liability — any agent asked to "check the history" fetches the whole thing and burns context. Archive to keep WORKLOG.md itself readable while preserving full history on disk.
   393	
   394	**Trigger** (soft threshold): WORKLOG.md exceeds **~1000 lines**. Measure by line count, not phase count — phase density varies ten-fold across projects, so lines are the reliable unit.
   395	
   396	**Archival procedure**:
   397	
   398	1. Decide the cut point: keep the most recent **3 phases** in `WORKLOG.md`; move earlier phases out.
   399	2. Create `WORKLOG_ARCHIVE_<YYYY-MM-DD>.md` where the date is **the archival event date** (i.e., today — the date you are performing the archival), not a fixed-period bin. Each archival event produces its own file, which keeps any single archive bounded (one archival moves at most the older portion of a ~1000-line WORKLOG). Multiple archive files accumulate chronologically over time. *Rationale for per-event vs. fixed-period naming: a project that accumulates 5,000 lines per quarter would otherwise put all 5,000 lines into one "quarterly" archive file, defeating the purpose of archival. Per-event naming makes each archive inherently bounded by the trigger threshold.*
   400	3. Move the older phase sections (including their entries in the TOC) to the archive file. The archive file has the same structure as WORKLOG.md (TOC at top + phase sections below).
   401	4. At the top of the archive file (above the archive's TOC), add a **backlink**:
   402	   ```
   403	   > Part of the WORKLOG series. Current WORKLOG: `WORKLOG.md`. Other archives: `WORKLOG_ARCHIVE_2025-12-03.md`, `WORKLOG_ARCHIVE_2026-02-14.md`, ...
   404	   ```
   405	   List the other archives in chronological order of the archival event.
   406	5. At the top of `WORKLOG.md`, add (or update) a **forward pointer** immediately under the title:
   407	   ```
   408	   > Earlier history archived in: `WORKLOG_ARCHIVE_2025-12-03.md`, `WORKLOG_ARCHIVE_2026-02-14.md`, `WORKLOG_ARCHIVE_2026-04-19.md`, ...
   409	   ```
   410	   Append the new archive to the existing list; keep chronological order.
   411	6. Register the new archive file in FILE_INDEX under a `## Archived History` category (create if missing). Existing archive entries stay; add one new entry for this archive.
   412	7. **Record the archival event in CURRENT_STATUS**. Add a one-line entry to the current phase's "Completed Steps" in the car body:
   413	   ```
   414	   - (YYYY-MM-DD) Archived WORKLOG: moved phases N–M into `WORKLOG_ARCHIVE_<YYYY-MM-DD>.md`; active WORKLOG now keeps the most recent 3 phases.
   415	   ```
   416	   This ensures a next-session agent, reading CURRENT_STATUS alone, sees that historical context has shifted to a new file — without having to diff WORKLOG.
   417	
   418	**Git commit convention**: Make the archival move a **single atomic commit** with message `Archive WORKLOG <YYYY-MM-DD> (keep most recent 3 phases)`. Do NOT squash the archive-creation commit with unrelated work — a future agent tracing history should be able to identify the archival event cleanly. Staging order inside the single commit: the new archive file is added, WORKLOG is edited, FILE_INDEX is edited, CURRENT_STATUS is edited — all in one commit.
   419	
   420	**Non-goals**: Archival is not deletion. Archive files are permanent records, never edited after creation except for errata. Never delete an archive file.
   421	
   422	**When to skip**: Projects with compact phases (e.g. ~20 lines each) may never trigger. That's fine; the threshold catches only projects that need it.
   423	
   424	---
   425	
   426	## Chapter 6: Information Flow Rules
   427	
   428	### 6.1 Daily Workflow
   429	
   430	```
   431	Read CLAUDE.md → Read CURRENT_STATUS → Start working
   432	During work:
   433	  ├── Complete meaningful step → update CURRENT_STATUS car body
   434	  ├── Create new file → register FILE_INDEX + record in CURRENT_STATUS car body
   435	  └── Session end → confirm car body reflects all work + update headlights + update date
   436	```
   437	
   438	### 6.2 Phase Transition (Five-Step Protocol)
   439	
   440	**Trigger conditions** (any one is sufficient):
   441	- Work goal fundamentally changes (e.g., "writing" → "reviewing")
   442	- User explicitly declares a new phase
   443	- Project pauses (>3 days without work)
   444	- Car body exceeds 200 lines
   445	
   446	**Does NOT trigger**: Sub-task switches within the same goal (e.g., Ch4→Ch5 within "literature reinforcement")
   447	
   448	**Five steps (execute in this order)**:
   449	
   450	```
   451	Step 1 (Protective — execute first):
   452	  Copy CURRENT_STATUS car body content in full to WORKLOG top (after TOC).
   453	  Add phase summary.
   454	  → After this step, even if interrupted, no data is lost.
   455	
   456	Step 2:
   457	  Insert new summary (3-5 lines) at top of CURRENT_STATUS tire tracks.
   458	  Note "Detailed record in WORKLOG § Phase N".
   459	
   460	Step 3:
   461	  If tire tracks exceed 3 → remove the oldest.
   462	
   463	Step 4:
   464	  Clear car body. Fill in new phase goal.
   465	  May include one brief context line.
   466	  Apply the driving-manual review ritual (see §6.2.2 below).
   467	
   468	Step 5:
   469	  Update CLAUDE.md "current phase" and "one-line status (as of date)".
   470	  Update WORKLOG TOC.
   471	```
   472	
   473	**Interrupt safety**: Step 1 executes first (copying content to WORKLOG), ensuring that even if compact occurs during Steps 2–5, data is safely preserved. Detection of an interrupted transition and the repair procedure are in §6.3.1.
   474	
   475	#### 6.2.1 Stepwise failure modes
   476	
   477	Each step has a characteristic failure signature. This table is for reference when diagnosing a malformed project state (see also §6.3.1):
   478	
   479	| Step | Failure signature | Repair |
   480	|------|-------------------|--------|
   481	| 1 | WORKLOG has no new entry; car body still full | No data risk yet — retry Step 1. |
   482	| 1 (partial) | WORKLOG has the detail block but no phase summary / no TOC row | Finish the summary from car body; add TOC row. |
   483	| 2 | CURRENT_STATUS tire tracks lack a new summary; WORKLOG has the entry | Insert the summary from WORKLOG into tire tracks. |
   484	| 3 | Tire tracks > 3 entries | Remove the oldest (it's permanent in WORKLOG). |
   485	| 4 | Car body still contains old phase content; new phase goal not written | Clear; write goal. |
   486	| 4 (partial) | Driving manual not reviewed | Apply §6.2.2 ritual. |
   487	| 5 | CLAUDE.md "current phase" still old; or WORKLOG TOC missing the new row | Update both. |
   488	
   489	A repair triggered during §6.3.1 mid-transition detection should perform these in order of downstream dependency, stopping when the project state is coherent again.
   490	
   491	#### 6.2.2 Driving-manual review ritual
   492	
   493	At Step 4 of every phase transition, walk the ritual below for each principle currently in the driving manual. This replaces ad-hoc judgment with a checklist.
   494	
   495	For each principle P in the current driving manual:
   496	
   497	1. **Is P marked `[DONE]` / `[已满足]`?**
   498	   → If the phase is ending (which it is, at a transition), **remove P**. Satisfied principles do not carry forward.
   499	
   500	2. **Has P been in the driving manual for ≥3 consecutive phases, with its semantic intent unchanged?**
   501	   "Unchanged" here means *the rule still says the same thing*, not literal text identity — rewording for clarity (rule 4) doesn't reset the counter. If in doubt, two principles carry the same intent when a violation of one would also be a violation of the other.
   502	   → **Candidate for promotion** to CLAUDE.md iron rules. Confirm by asking: would violating P in any future phase be a real problem? If yes, promote. Record the promotion in the WORKLOG phase-transition entry.
   503	
   504	3. **Does P respond to a constraint that no longer exists?** (e.g., "always use library X" after the project migrated off X)
   505	   → **Remove P**.
   506	
   507	4. **Does P apply to the NEW phase's expected work?**
   508	   → **Keep P** as-is. Optionally rewrite for clarity if the new phase context changes how P reads.
   509	
   510	5. **Does P apply to only some sub-tasks of the new phase?**
   511	   → **Keep P**, but consider annotating the narrower scope.
   512	
   513	Then add new principles specific to the new phase's work. Expect 1–4 principles per phase; a driving manual with >6 entries is usually a sign of overfitting — prune.
   514	
   515	### 6.3 Context Compact Recovery
   516	
   517	```
   518	Compact occurs
   519	  → Read CLAUDE.md → understand project and recovery chain
   520	  → Read CURRENT_STATUS.md:
   521	      Tire tracks → "what was recently completed"
   522	      Car body → "what's the current state"
   523	      Headlights → "what to do next"
   524	      Driving manual → "what to watch out for"
   525	  → Run §6.3.1 Mid-Transition Detection (below)
   526	  → Continue working (if user is present, confirm whether next steps have changed)
   527	```
   528	
   529	#### 6.3.1 Mid-Transition Detection and Repair
   530	
   531	A phase transition can be interrupted between Step 1 and Step 5 (compaction, crash, manual interruption). The symptom depends on which step completed. Run this three-way coherence check at every session start:
   532	
   533	**Three values to compare**:
   534	- **A** — CLAUDE.md "current phase" string.
   535	- **B** — WORKLOG TOC's newest entry (top row, after the TOC header).
   536	- **C** — CURRENT_STATUS tire tracks' newest phase summary (first `###` heading under "Recent Completed").
   537	
   538	**Coherence rules**:
   539	
   540	| A | B | C | State | Action |
   541	|---|---|---|-------|--------|
   542	| Phase N | Phase N (old) | Phase N−1 newest | ✅ Healthy mid-phase | Proceed. |
   543	| ⏸️ | any | any | Paused — possibly mid-transition | Apply §6.4 resume rules; detection resumes there. |
   544	| Phase N+1 | Phase N | Phase N−1 newest | ❌ Step 1 incomplete (phase title updated early but WORKLOG not written) | **Should never happen** if agents follow the 5-step order. If detected, protect data: re-read CURRENT_STATUS car body, treat as in-flight Phase N, execute Step 1 now. |
   545	| Phase N | Phase N (new) | Phase N−1 newest | ❌ Step 2 incomplete (WORKLOG has new Phase N entry from Step 1 but tire tracks not updated) | Copy the phase summary from WORKLOG's new entry to the top of CURRENT_STATUS tire tracks; if tire tracks now exceed 3, run Step 3. Then proceed to Step 4. |
   546	| Phase N | Phase N (new) | Phase N−1 newest, tire tracks >3 | ❌ Step 3 incomplete | Remove the oldest tire track entry. Then proceed to Step 4. |
   547	| Phase N (old) | Phase N (new) | Phase N (new) newest | ❌ Step 5 incomplete (WORKLOG and tire tracks advanced but CLAUDE.md still shows old phase) | Update CLAUDE.md "current phase" and "one-line status (as of date)"; update WORKLOG TOC if missing the row. |
   548	| Any other inconsistency | — | — | ⚠️ Ambiguous | Write the diagnostic to CURRENT_STATUS car body as a `#### Mid-transition detected (YYYY-MM-DD)` entry. If user is present → ask. Otherwise → complete the transition in the direction WORKLOG points (WORKLOG is authoritative for "what was intended"). |
   549	
   550	**Footnote on "Phase N" in column B**: "Phase N (old)" means B points at the *current* phase's WORKLOG entry (written when Phase N began). "Phase N (new)" means B points at a *newly-written* entry for an incoming Phase N that signals Step 1 completed for a transition *out of* Phase N−1. The distinguisher is the relationship to C: when C is Phase N−1 (the healthy predecessor), B=Phase N is the stable mid-phase entry; when C is Phase N−1 *and* there is a new Phase N row at B with contents that don't match CURRENT_STATUS car body, Step 1 of a transition wrote B but the rest didn't land. Agents implement the table by checking string equality of phase names and date fields, not by semantic interpretation.
   551	
   552	**Zero-progress Step 1 interrupt**: the table cannot detect an interrupt that happened *before* any writes landed in WORKLOG (A, B, C all still reflect the pre-transition state). This is not a data-loss scenario — no transition state exists yet — but the next agent should be cautious about extending the car body with new work if the phase goal is approaching a transition boundary. When in doubt, the agent should check whether §6.2's trigger conditions already met before compaction; if yes, initiate a fresh phase transition rather than prolonging the old phase.
   553	
   554	**After any repair action**: add one line to CURRENT_STATUS car body noting the repair (e.g., `#### Auto-repaired phase transition Step 2 on 2026-04-19 during compact recovery`). Do not write more than one such line per compact — subsequent edits belong to normal work.
   555	
   556	**Why this works**: Step 1 (data to WORKLOG) is protective — no real state is lost once Step 1 completes. Steps 2–5 are bookkeeping that can be finished deterministically from the WORKLOG state. The only dangerous case (first row in the table) is impossible if agents follow the 5-step order; detection exists for paranoia only.
   557	
   558	### 6.4 Project Pause and Resume
   559	
   560	#### Pausing (orderly)
   561	
   562	1. Execute the five-step phase transition (save current work to WORKLOG).
   563	2. Write in CURRENT_STATUS car body: `Project paused on YYYY-MM-DD. Reason: ...`
   564	3. Update CLAUDE.md status to ⏸️ and refresh the one-line status.
   565	4. Write down, in the car body pause note, any **time-sensitive context** that would invalidate headlights on resume (e.g., "depends on X deliverable expected 2026-05-15; confirm X state before acting on headlights").
   566	
   567	#### Pausing (emergency / mid-phase-transition)
   568	
   569	If the pause itself interrupts a phase transition (rare, but possible), do **not** try to finish the transition first — that risks losing data under time pressure. Instead:
   570	
   571	1. Write `Project paused on YYYY-MM-DD (during phase transition, Step N reached)` in whichever document is safest to edit (usually CURRENT_STATUS car body; fall back to CLAUDE.md one-line status if car body is also in an inconsistent state).
   572	2. Set CLAUDE.md status to ⏸️.
   573	3. On resume, §6.3.1 mid-transition detection will identify the interrupted state and repair it before normal work resumes.
   574	
   575	#### Resuming (user present)
   576	
   577	1. Agent reads CLAUDE.md → sees ⏸️.
   578	2. Reads CURRENT_STATUS → tire tracks have the last phase summary, car body has pause notice.
   579	3. Reads WORKLOG latest phase → gets complete pre-pause work details.
   580	4. **Critical**: Headlights "next steps" may be stale. Confirm with user before executing. Pay particular attention to any time-sensitive context recorded at pause time.
   581	5. Flip CLAUDE.md status from ⏸️ to ⏳; refresh one-line status.
   582	
   583	#### Resuming (no user present — auto-resume)
   584	
   585	Invoked when an agent is compacted back into a paused project without direct user input.
   586	
   587	1. Agent reads CLAUDE.md → sees ⏸️.
   588	2. Reads pause note in car body; notes pause date.
   589	3. **Run §6.3.1 mid-transition detection FIRST.** If a mid-transition state is detected, **repair it before any resume decision**. The pause may itself have occurred during a phase transition (see emergency-pause path above); resuming into such a project without repairing first risks acting on inconsistent state.
   590	4. Only after §6.3.1 returns a coherent state, **compare pause date to today**:
   591	   - **≤7 days** (pause date is today, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, or 7 days ago): likely resumable. Check headlights against time-sensitive context (if any). If everything looks current, write a car body entry `#### Auto-resumed on YYYY-MM-DD (user absent)`, flip CLAUDE.md to ⏳, and continue per headlights.
   592	   - **8–30 days**: headlights are suspect. Do NOT execute headlights silently. Write `#### Auto-resume attempted YYYY-MM-DD — waiting for user confirmation` in car body. Leave CLAUDE.md at ⏸️. At the next user interaction, raise the question.
   593	   - **>30 days**: never auto-resume. Always wait for explicit user direction.
   594	
   595	---
   596	
   597	## Chapter 7: Single Source of Truth
   598	
   599	### 7.1 Core Rule
   600	
   601	**Each fact is maintained in only one document.**
   602	
   603	| Fact Type | Sole Source |
   604	|-----------|------------|
   605	| Current state/progress/numbers | CURRENT_STATUS.md |
   606	| File catalog/locations | FILE_INDEX.md |
   607	| Historical work details | WORKLOG.md |
   608	| Project overview/entry/iron rules | CLAUDE.md |
   609	
   610	### 7.2 Only Allowed Redundancy
   611	
   612	CLAUDE.md's "one-line status (as of date)". Must include a date stamp; if contradicted, CURRENT_STATUS is authoritative.
   613	
   614	---
   615	
   616	## Chapter 8: Two-Level Principle Management
   617	
   618	### 8.1 Two Types of Principles
   619	
   620	| Type | Location | Lifecycle | Example |
   621	|------|----------|-----------|---------|
   622	| **Project-level iron rules** | CLAUDE.md "Iron Rules" section | Lives with project | "Never read paper .md files directly" |
   623	| **Phase-level principles** | CURRENT_STATUS "Driving Manual" | Lives and dies with phase | "Compile LaTeX after every edit this phase" |
   624	
   625	### 8.2 Promotion and Demotion
   626	
   627	- At phase transition, check if any driving manual principles **should be promoted to iron rules**
   628	- If a principle appears in 3 consecutive phases, it likely should be promoted
   629	- Promotion: move from driving manual to CLAUDE.md iron rules section
   630	- Demotion is rare — once established, iron rules generally persist
   631	
   632	### 8.3 Iron Rule Management
   633	
   634	Iron rules live in CLAUDE.md and persist for the project's lifetime. New iron rules may be added at phase transitions (promoted from driving manual). Iron rules are generally not deleted — if preconditions no longer apply, annotate "[No longer applicable: reason]" but keep the original text for historical reference.
   635	
   636	---
   637	
   638	## Chapter 9: Document Lifecycle
   639	
   640	### 9.1 Core Status Documents
   641	The four core documents live as long as the project.
   642	
   643	### 9.2 Leaf Documents
   644	
   645	| State | Meaning | Marking |
   646	|-------|---------|---------|
   647	| Active | In use or still valid | Default (no marking needed) |
   648	| SUPERSEDED (retained) | Replaced, but still has reference value | First line: `⚠️ SUPERSEDED BY [new document]`. Move to `## Superseded` category in FILE_INDEX. |
   649	| SUPERSEDED (archived) | Replaced and no longer needed | First line: `⚠️ SUPERSEDED BY [new document]`. Move to _archive/. Remove from FILE_INDEX. |
   650	| ARCHIVED | Historical, moved to _archive/ | Remove from FILE_INDEX |
   651	
   652	Most superseded documents in practice are **retained** because they contain valuable reference information (e.g., original README with style guides, old STATUS with detailed session logs). Use the "retained" option unless the document truly has no remaining value.
   653	
   654	---
   655	
   656	## Chapter 10: Sub-projects and Project Groups
   657	
   658	### 10.1 Sub-projects
   659	Sub-projects have their own complete four-document system; all rules apply recursively. The parent project's FILE_INDEX registers the sub-project entry point.
   660	
   661	### 10.2 Project Groups
   662	When multiple independent projects share a parent directory, the parent may have a lightweight CLAUDE.md (navigation table only — no CURRENT_STATUS/FILE_INDEX/WORKLOG).
   663	
   664	```markdown
   665	# [Workspace] — Project Navigation
   666	
   667	## Active Projects
   668	| Project | Entry | Status |
   669	|---------|-------|--------|
   670	| Project A | [CLAUDE.md](A/CLAUDE.md) | ⏳ |
   671	| Project B | [CLAUDE.md](B/CLAUDE.md) | ⏸️ |
   672	
   673	## Shared Infrastructure
   674	| Tool | Path | Description |
   675	|------|------|-------------|
   676	
   677	## Archived Projects
   678	| Project | Path | Completion Date |
   679	|---------|------|----------------|
   680	```
   681	
   682	When an agent arrives at a project group, the user's instructions typically determine which sub-project to enter.
   683	
   684	---
   685	
   686	## Chapter 10.3: Adapting to Existing Projects
   687	
   688	**Core principle: Doc Harness adapts to the project, not the other way around.**
   689	
   690	### Mid-Project Adoption
   691	
   692	Most real-world adoption happens mid-project — the project already has files, possibly existing status documents, and a history of work. The process:
   693	
   694	1. **Understand the project first.** Read all existing status/readme documents thoroughly before creating Doc Harness files. Understand the project's goals, current state, directory structure, and what documentation already exists.
   695	
   696	2. **Create the four core documents.** CLAUDE.md, CURRENT_STATUS.md, FILE_INDEX.md, WORKLOG.md — populated with the project's actual current state, not blank templates.
   697	
   698	3. **Handle existing status documents.** Most should be marked SUPERSEDED but retained:
   699	   - Add `⚠️ SUPERSEDED BY [new doc]` at the first line
   700	   - Move to the `## Superseded` category in FILE_INDEX
   701	   - Note why it's retained (e.g., "contains detailed session logs" or "has style guide reference")
   702	
   703	4. **Reconstruct WORKLOG from history.** Use existing logs, status docs, and git history to build phase records. Mark reconstructed sections: "(Reconstructed from [source document])". The goal is useful history, not perfect accuracy — real-time records will always be more detailed.
   704	
   705	5. **Preserve existing high-quality indexes.** If a sub-directory already has a well-maintained index (e.g., a research analysis INDEX.md with 100+ entries and status labels), FILE_INDEX.md should **point to it** rather than rebuild it. Add a line like: `→ See [subdir/INDEX.md] (N entries, covers [scope])`.
   706	
   707	### Sub-Index Guidelines for Large Directories
   708	
   709	For directories with more than 20 files, create a sub-FILE_INDEX.md. For initial creation of large sub-indexes (100+ files), automated file-system scanning can generate the initial structure, which should then be manually verified and annotated where possible.
   710	
   711	---
   712	
   713	## Chapter 11: Agent Behavior Guidelines
   714	
   715	### 11.1 Session Start — Applying Recovery Chain
   716	
   717	Follow the project's Recovery Chain (defined in CLAUDE.md §Recovery Chain):
   718	
   719	1. Read the **must-read** layer in order (CLAUDE.md → CURRENT_STATUS.md, typically 2–3 files).
   720	2. Scan the **task-conditional** layer. Read only the entries whose condition matches the current work.
   721	3. If user is present → confirm whether next steps have changed.
   722	4. If compact recovery (user not present) → continue per headlights.
   723	
   724	Do not unconditionally read all task-conditional entries at startup. That defeats the purpose of the two-layer split. If you find yourself reading a file every session, it probably belongs in must-read — promote it explicitly.
   725	
   726	### 11.2 During Work
   727	
   728	1. Complete a **meaningful step** → update CURRENT_STATUS car body
   729	2. Create a new file → **do two things simultaneously**: (1) register in FILE_INDEX (2) record in CURRENT_STATUS car body
   730	3. **"Write It Down"**: important analysis results, design ideas, decision rationale → save to file + register
   731	4. **Watch remaining context** (if exposed by the runtime): context compression is involuntary session end. If your environment reports a context-usage percentage or token count, treat **low remaining context** (~<20%) as an immediate trigger — update CURRENT_STATUS before the next tool call; if the car body has **substantial unsaved work**, consider a phase transition now. Don't wait for a "meaningful step" that may never land.
   732	
   733	   **"Substantial unsaved work" — concrete threshold** (any one suffices): (a) ≥3 completed `####` step headings since the last car-body flush; (b) ≥50 lines added to the car body since the last flush; (c) car body ≥100 lines (half the 200-line phase-transition threshold). If none of (a)–(c) apply, just flush — don't force a phase transition from a thin car body.
   734	
   735	### 11.3 Session End
   736	
   737	1. Ensure CURRENT_STATUS car body reflects all work from this session
   738	2. Update headlights "next steps"
   739	3. Update CURRENT_STATUS "last updated" date
   740	4. Update CLAUDE.md "one-line status (as of date)"
   741	5. Check: are all files created this session registered in FILE_INDEX?
   742	6. Check: is there any important information only in context? → Write it down!
   743	7. If a phase transition occurred: check WORKLOG length — over ~1000 lines? → trigger archival per §5.5.
   744	
   745	### 11.4 Phase Transition
   746	
   747	Execute the five-step protocol defined in Chapter 6 §6.2.
   748	
   749	### 11.5 Status Sync (`/doc-harness sync`)
   750	
   751	**Purpose**: Actively repair documentation drift. Unlike `check` (read-only diagnosis), `sync` modifies files to bring them back into alignment with reality.
   752	
   753	**Trigger conditions**:
   754	- User explicitly requests a sync
   755	- Agent detects significant drift during session-end checklist
   756	- Before a long project pause
   757	- After bulk file operations outside normal agent workflow
   758	
   759	**Modes**:
   760	- **`auto`** (default): Execute all safe fixes (file registration, date refresh) without asking. If car body ≥200 lines or WORKLOG ≥1000 lines, auto-executes phase transition or archival per spec §6.2 and §5.5.
   761	- **`interactive`**: Same fixes, but asks user before phase transitions, archival, or creating new principle documents from context.
   762	
   763	**Procedure**: See `sync.md` for the complete step-by-step procedure (drift scan → auto fixes → phase-transition check → archival check → principle extraction).
   764	
   765	**Relationship to `check`**: `check` reports; `sync` repairs. Run `check` to understand the full health picture; run `sync` to fix drift. `sync` does NOT perform principle reflection — that remains `check`'s domain.
   766	
   767	### 11.6 Context Flush (`/doc-harness flush`)
   768	
   769	**Purpose**: Emergency save before context compression or session end. Includes everything `sync` does, plus mandatory extraction of important context information into documents.
   770	
   771	**Core guarantee**: After a successful flush, a new agent reading the Recovery Chain should recover project state **as if context had never been compressed** — knowing *what information exists* and *where to find it*.
   772	
   773	**Trigger conditions**:
   774	- User explicitly requests a flush ("save everything," "prepare for compact")
   775	- Context usage is high and user wants to ensure zero loss
   776	- Before a known context reset
   777	- After a long, high-density session with significant context accumulation
   778	
   779	**Modes**:
   780	- **`auto`** (default): Uses heuristics to classify context information by type and route it to appropriate documents (`notes/`, `design/`, `PHILOSOPHY.md`, etc.) without asking.
   781	- **`interactive`**: Proposes each extraction to the user for approval or path editing.
   782	
   783	**Procedure** (five phases):
   784	1. **Phase A**: Run `sync` in the same mode.
   785	2. **Phase B**: Context inventory — agent self-scans context, classifies items by type, skips items already durable (in car body or FILE_INDEX).
   786	3. **Phase C**: Write and register — create or append files, register in FILE_INDEX, record in car body.
   787	4. **Phase D**: Verification — agent simulates a fresh arrival to confirm all extracted information is discoverable.
   788	5. **Phase E**: Flush marker — record the flush event in CURRENT_STATUS car body.
   789	
   790	**Auto-mode heuristics**: Information is "important" if user-emphasized, a decision/rationale, required significant effort to produce, or would cause confusion if lost. Target paths follow existing project conventions; standard folders (`notes/`, `design/`, `lessons/`, `data/`) are created only when needed.
   791	
   792	**Full procedure**: See `flush.md`.
   793	
   794	---
   795	
   796	## Chapter 12: Anti-patterns
   797	
   798	| Anti-pattern | Correct Approach |
   799	|-------------|-----------------|
   800	| Same number hardcoded in multiple documents | Maintain only in CURRENT_STATUS; others reference it |
   801	| Superseded document not marked | Add SUPERSEDED notice at first line |
   802	| Multiple recovery chains | Recovery chain defined only in CLAUDE.md |
   803	| Recovery Chain references agent-side features (memory / chat history / external services) | Recovery Chain must be self-contained — only project-internal files |
   804	| Recovery Chain must-read layer grows past 3 entries | Demote extras to task-conditional; must-read stays lean |
   805	| File created but not registered | Register in FILE_INDEX immediately on creation |
   806	| CURRENT_STATUS grows indefinitely | Transfer details to WORKLOG at phase transitions |
   807	| WORKLOG grows past ~1000 lines untouched | Archive per §5.5 |
   808	| Information exists only in context | "Write It Down" — save to file and register |
   809	| Phase principles become permanent legacy | Review at phase transition: promote to iron rule or remove |
   810	| WORKLOG has no table of contents | Maintain TOC table at top |
   811	
   812	---
   813	
   814	## Chapter 13: Optional Long-Horizon Documents
   815	
   816	The four core documents (CLAUDE / CURRENT_STATUS / FILE_INDEX / WORKLOG) are tuned for short-to-medium-horizon work flow: what's the current phase, what got done, where are the files, what's the history. Two categories of information don't fit well in any of them. Doc Harness offers two **optional** documents for these, used only when a project genuinely accumulates such content.
   817	
   818	These documents are opt-in. A project that doesn't need them should not create them.
   819	
   820	### 13.1 PARKING_LOT.md — Deferred Items
   821	
   822	**Purpose**: Concrete things you'd like to do but can't right now. Without a parking lot, such items either clutter CURRENT_STATUS headlights (wrong — they're not next) or get overwritten by new work and forgotten.
   823	
   824	**When to create**: When a specific item is being removed from active consideration but shouldn't be lost. Typical trigger: during phase transition, some driving manual principle or next-step item is no longer for *now* but will be relevant again under known conditions.
   825	
   826	**Entry format**: Each entry records **what** to do, **why it's deferred**, **preconditions for revival**, and **when to re-check**.
   827	
   828	```markdown
   829	## Entries
   830	
   831	### [Item title] — deferred YYYY-MM-DD
   832	- **What**: [concrete action or goal]
   833	- **Why deferred**: [reason — e.g., "depends on X which won't ship until Q3"]
   834	- **Preconditions for revival**: [what must be true before this can resume]
   835	- **Re-check**: [date or event — e.g., "check at next phase transition" or "2026-09-01"]
   836	```
   837	
   838	**Lifecycle**: When preconditions become true, either (a) move the item to CURRENT_STATUS headlights, striking from PARKING_LOT; or (b) keep the entry and annotate with a decision — e.g., "[Revived 2026-09-15 → now active]" or "[No longer relevant 2026-09-15 because X]". Never silently delete.
   839	
   840	**Recovery Chain integration**: Add to the task-conditional layer, e.g. `- If planning a new phase: read PARKING_LOT.md (any deferred items revivable?)`.
   841	
   842	### 13.2 PHILOSOPHY.md — Principles From Practice
   843	
   844	**Purpose**: Record principles, lessons, and generalizable insights that emerge from the project's specific practice. These are broader than iron rules (which govern *this* project's operations) and more durable than the driving manual (which governs *this phase*).
   845	
   846	**Design rationale**: General wisdom is born from specific practice. The project is the forge; the principle is what comes out. Forbidding projects from recording their own philosophy severs the principle from its origin. PHILOSOPHY.md is that capture layer.
   847	
   848	**When to create**: When working on the project surfaces an insight you suspect generalizes beyond the immediate situation — a reusable lesson, a design trade-off worth remembering, a mistake pattern you don't want to repeat.
   849	
   850	**Entry format**: Each entry states the principle, the practice that forged it, and the first-recorded date.
   851	
   852	```markdown
   853	## Principles
   854	
   855	### [Short principle name] — first recorded YYYY-MM-DD
   856	**Principle**: [one-sentence statement of the principle]
   857	
   858	**Forged by**: [the specific practice / incident / observation that produced this — be concrete about *what happened* that led to this lesson]
   859	
   860	**Scope**: [where this applies — this project only? likely broader? already confirmed broader?]
   861	```
   862	
   863	**Sharing across projects (optional)**: When a principle turns out to apply beyond this project, it may be copied into a sibling project's own `PHILOSOPHY.md`, or (if a parent navigation CLAUDE.md exists over a project group — see Chapter 10) referenced there. Copying/referencing **does not remove** the entry from this project's `PHILOSOPHY.md` — each project that adopted the principle keeps its own birthplace record, and this file documents how *this* project arrived at it. Annotate shared entries with `[Also adopted by <project> YYYY-MM-DD]` for traceability.
   864	
   865	**Lifecycle**: Principles may be refined with errata (`[Refined YYYY-MM-DD: ...]`) or marked superseded (`[Superseded YYYY-MM-DD by: new formulation]`), but entries are not deleted. A PHILOSOPHY.md is read rarely but should survive intact.
   866	
   867	**Recovery Chain integration**: Add to task-conditional layer for reflective decisions, e.g. `- If making a major architectural decision: read PHILOSOPHY.md`.
   868	
   869	---
   870	
   871	## Chapter 14: Optional Inter-Project Communication (inbox/outbox)
   872	
   873	When a project operates alongside other projects that depend on it or that it depends on, cross-project information (requirements, deliverables, status changes, confirmations) must persist across session boundaries. Verbal/chat-only exchange is lost when a session ends; the recipient project's next agent has no way to discover it. Doc Harness offers an **optional** file-based protocol for this.
   874	
   875	This entire chapter is **self-contained** — a project that adopts it needs no documentation beyond this chapter and its own `DOC_HARNESS_SPEC.md`. No external protocol file required, no dependency on any parent folder or sibling project. A project that does NOT adopt it is unaffected.
   876	
   877	### 14.1 When to adopt
   878	
   879	Adopt if any of the following is true:
   880	- This project has a dependency on another project (e.g., consumes data, an API, or deliverables from it).
   881	- Another project depends on this one.
   882	- Cross-project coordination happens repeatedly (decisions, requirements, numbers exchanged more than once).
   883	
   884	Skip if the project is truly standalone.
   885	
   886	### 14.2 Folder structure
   887	
   888	Two directories at the project root:
   889	
   890	```
   891	project_root/
   892	├── inbox/        ← messages addressed TO this project
   893	├── outbox/       ← messages sent FROM this project (drafts / sent-copies)
   894	└── ... (rest of project)
   895	```
   896	
   897	Both start empty. Git-track them by adding a `.gitkeep` (or equivalent) if your VCS requires it.
   898	
   899	### 14.3 Message format
   900	
   901	**Filename**: `YYYY-MM-DD-from-<source-project>-<topic-slug>.md`
   902	
   903	- `<source-project>`: short identifier of the sender (e.g. `whoami`, `smss`).
   904	- `<topic-slug>`: kebab-case summary of the topic.
   905	- Example: `2026-04-19-from-whoami-skill-improvement-proposals.md`.
   906	
   907	**Disambiguator for same-day collisions**: if a filename would collide with one already present (same date + same source + same topic), append `-HHMMSS` (sender's local time, zero-padded) before `.md`. Example: `2026-04-19-from-whoami-skill-improvement-proposals-143052.md`. The sender checks its own outbox for collisions before writing; if found, include HHMMSS on the new message and leave the existing one unchanged. Recipients treat the disambiguated filename as a distinct message.
   908	
   909	**Sub-second collisions**: on rare occasions (automated senders issuing multiple messages per second) a `-HHMMSS` name may itself collide. If the check still finds a collision after applying `-HHMMSS`, further disambiguate by appending `-<N>` where `N` is the smallest positive integer that produces a unique name (e.g., `...-143052-2.md`). This is the terminal rule — do not fall back to overwriting. §14.8's "multiple messages with the same filename" row handles the pathological case where a collision still occurs despite these rules (e.g., two senders writing independently); the on-disk file wins and the sender is alerted via `/doc-harness check` §1.7.
   910	
   911	**Header** (YAML frontmatter, required):
   912	
   913	```yaml
   914	---
   915	from: <source project name>
   916	to: <target project name>
   917	date: YYYY-MM-DD
   918	subject: <one-line subject>
   919	status: unread | read | actioned
   920	in-reply-to: <original filename, if this message is a reply; else null>
   921	priority: low | normal | high
   922	---
   923	```
   924	
   925	**Body**: free-form Markdown. Tables, checklists, code blocks permitted.
   926	
   927	### 14.3.1 Pre-send verification (sender's responsibility)
   928	
   929	Before writing a new message to a recipient's `inbox/`, the sender **must** verify that the recipient has the inbox/outbox protocol active. Otherwise delivery is silent-failure: a file lands in a directory the recipient never scans, or the copy fails with `ENOENT` on a nonexistent target.
   930	
   931	Verification steps (in order, stop at first failure):
   932	1. **Target path exists**: the recipient project directory exists and is reachable from the sender.
   933	2. **Recipient's `inbox/` exists**: if absent, the recipient has not adopted the protocol (or is no longer participating). **Do not create `inbox/` in the recipient's project** — that would silently opt them in without consent.
   934	3. **Recipient's CLAUDE.md contains the inter-project iron rule block** (grep for the string `inbox/` in recipient CLAUDE.md). This confirms the recipient's next agent will actually scan its inbox.
   935	
   936	**If any step fails**: do NOT copy the file to recipient's `inbox/`. Instead:
   937	- Write the message to your own `outbox/` as normal (permanent record).
   938	- Record the failed delivery in CURRENT_STATUS car body: `#### Attempted to send <topic> to <recipient> on YYYY-MM-DD — recipient has not adopted inbox/outbox protocol. Message held in own outbox only.`
   939	- Raise the issue with the user at the next opportunity. Do not retry automatically.
   940	
   941	### 14.4 Message lifecycle and rules
   942	
   943	```
   944	Sender                                        Recipient
   945	  │                                              │
   946	  ├─ writes new message to own outbox/           │
   947	  ├─ copies the same file into recipient inbox/  │
   948	  │  (status: unread, set by sender)             │
   949	  │                                              │
   950	  │   ─── session boundary ───                   │
   951	  │                                              │
   952	  │                      recipient's Recovery ──┤
   953	  │                      Chain points to inbox/ ─┤
   954	  │                      recipient reads msg    ─┤
   955	  │                      → status: read         ─┤
   956	  │                      performs any action    ─┤
   957	  │                      → status: actioned     ─┤
   958	  │                      (if reply needed:      ─┤
   959	  │                       sends a NEW message)  ─┤
   960	```
   961	
   962	**Rules**:
   963	
   964	1. **Received messages are immutable** — never edit a file in your `inbox/` beyond updating the `status` field. To respond, write a new message.
   965	2. **Status transitions** — sender sets `unread` at delivery. Recipient changes to `read` after reading, then to `actioned` after completing any required action. An `actioned` message with no required action is equivalent to acknowledged-and-closed.
   966	3. **Archival** — messages older than 30 days with `status: actioned` **should** be moved to `inbox/_archive/` (same structure inside). The archival audit runs as part of `/doc-harness check` §1.7 — when the check finds ≥5 actioned messages older than 30 days, it flags archival as an action item; the agent performs the move during the same session. Archived messages are permanent records; do not delete.
   967	4. **Sender retains a copy** — the sender's `outbox/` is the permanent draft/record. If the recipient loses their copy, the sender's `outbox/` is authoritative for what was sent.
   968	5. **Cross-project reference snapshots** — when communicating numbers, deliverables, or state ("our model reached accuracy 0.88"), send a **snapshot** in an inbox message rather than pointing the recipient at your internal files. Internal files churn and refactors break external references. A snapshot, once delivered, does not lie.
   969	
   970	### 14.5 Integration with the four core documents
   971	
   972	**CLAUDE.md** — add one iron rule block (copy-paste template, no customization required):
   973	
   974	```markdown
   975	**Inter-project communication via inbox/outbox (file-based protocol)**
   976	
   977	- **Mechanism**: This project maintains `inbox/` (received messages) and `outbox/` (sent messages). Messages are Markdown files with YAML frontmatter; filename `YYYY-MM-DD-from-<source>-<topic>.md`.
   978	- **Why this is mandatory (if adopted)**: Cross-project information exchanged only in chat is lost on session end. File-based messages survive session boundaries and are discoverable by any future agent through this project's Recovery Chain.
   979	- **Receiving**: Recovery Chain checks `inbox/` for `status: unread`. Read → update to `status: read`. After acting on the message → `status: actioned`. Never edit received messages beyond the status field; to respond, write a new message.
   980	- **Sending**: Write to this project's `outbox/` (permanent sender-side record) AND copy the same file into the recipient project's `inbox/`. Record the exchange in CURRENT_STATUS so it is traceable next session.
   981	- **Snapshots over pointers**: When communicating numbers/deliverables to another project, put the value in the message body rather than referencing internal files.
   982	- **Full specification**: `DOC_HARNESS_SPEC.md` §14 (in this project's root).
   983	```
   984	
   985	**CURRENT_STATUS.md** — when an incoming message requires action, add it to Headlights:
   986	
   987	```markdown
   988	### Immediate Actions
   989	- [ ] Respond to <sender>'s <topic> (see `inbox/YYYY-MM-DD-from-<source>-<topic>.md`)
   990	```
   991	
   992	Also record outbound exchanges in the car body as they happen:
   993	
   994	```markdown
   995	#### Sent deliverable to <target> (YYYY-MM-DD)
   996	- Message: `outbox/YYYY-MM-DD-from-<this-project>-<topic>.md` (same filename convention as §14.3 — the outbox file has the same name as the copy sent to the recipient's inbox)
   997	- Summary: <one line>
   998	```
   999	
  1000	**FILE_INDEX.md** — register both directories under their own category:


</details>
