计划已完成并通过审核。核心结论：

---

## 🔍 调研结论

**根本原因**：Agent 身份混乱不是"操作失误"，而是**认知漂移**——深度阅读其他项目代码后，agent 的自我认知被潜移默化了。现有的 Iron Rules、Recovery Chain、inbox/outbox 规范都是**行为约束**（"不要做什么"），但缺了一个**认知锚定**（"你是谁"）。

**四个替代方案全部否决**，只有一个推荐：

- ❌ 只加 check 警告（被动，不治本）
- ❌ 新建 `IDENTITY.md` 文件（破坏 must-read 精简原则）
- ❌ 放进 Iron Rules（规则是行为规范，身份是认知状态）
- ✅ **CLAUDE.md 最顶部放 `🔒 AGENT IDENTITY LOCK`**（WhoAMI 实战验证有效）

---

## 🎯 推荐方案：v1.6.0

| 变更 | 位置 | 说明 |
|------|------|------|
| **AGENT IDENTITY LOCK** | CLAUDE.md 最顶部 | 两层模板：基础版（所有项目）+ 扩展版（inbox/outbox 项目） |
| **Step 0 身份锚定** | Recovery Chain session start | "在读取任何文件之前，先确认你是 X 项目的代理" |
| **Pre-send Checklist** | spec §14.3.2 | 5 项自检：from 字段、outbox 路径、inbox 路径、未改对方文档、协议已激活 |
| **Identity Lock 验证** | check §1.11 + §2.5 | 检查 CLAUDE.md 前 30 行是否包含身份锁 |

**影响 14 个文件**，双语同步，向后兼容（现有项目不报错，只提示推荐补充）。

---

计划文件已保存到 `C:\Users\ZY\.kimi\plans\nightwing-valkyrie-aquaman.md`。

**等你的指令：是否开始实施 v1.6.0？**

## Turn 4

### User

很好。这样的思路可能会导致这样的场景：
1. 一个agent到来，面临空的context。系统（或者用户）提示它读claude.md
2. 它明白了这是个什么项目，我将作为哪个项目的参与者（主agent）参与执行该项目。

### Assistant

<details><summary>Thinking</summary>

用户在确认我的分析方向是对的。他描述了一个场景：agent 到来，读 CLAUDE.md，明白项目身份。这说明他认同 AGENT IDENTITY LOCK 的核心思路。

他继续说"但是..."或者只是确认思路。让我等他说完。

实际上用户没有说完，他只是描述了一个理想场景。让我顺着这个思路，把场景补充完整，确认我理解了他的意图，然后询问是否需要开始实施。

</details>

是的，这正是 AGENT IDENTITY LOCK 要保障的**黄金路径**：

```
空 context → 读 CLAUDE.md → 第一眼看到 🔒 AGENT IDENTITY LOCK
            → "我是 doc-harness 项目的代理"
            → 接着读 Recovery Chain、项目概述、铁律...
            → 所有后续认知都被"我是 doc-harness"的框架过滤
```

**没有这把锁时的危险路径**：

```
空 context → 读 CLAUDE.md → 读 CURRENT_STATUS → 用户说"调查一下 lit 的 Q4 问题"
            → 深度阅读 lit-system-api 代码 30 分钟
            → context 中 lit 的文件占主导
            → 认知漂移："我好像是在维护 lit..."
            → 向 lit/outbox/ 写入文件（错误）
```

**有这把锁时的修正路径**：

```
...深度阅读 lit 代码 30 分钟后...
→ 准备写入 lit/outbox/
→ 内心触发 Step 0 锚定："等等，我是 doc-harness 的代理，不是 lit 的"
→ 重新读 CLAUDE.md 顶部的锁
→ 行为纠正：写入 WhoAMI/outbox/ + 复制到 lit/inbox/
```

这把锁的本质是**给 agent 一个不可覆盖的第一帧**——无论后续 context 里进了多少其他项目的信息，"我是谁"这个答案在到达时就写死了。

---

需要我现在开始按 plan 实施 v1.6.0 吗？还是你有其他想调整的地方？

## Turn 5

### User

不如在每次执行doc-harness的指令时，都确定一下自己属于哪个项目？这样，每次维护状态文档系统，自己的身份信息就会出现在context中，有助于llm保持对自己身份的认知。

### Assistant

<details><summary>Thinking</summary>

用户提出了一个很好的改进建议：与其只在 CLAUDE.md 顶部放一次性的 AGENT IDENTITY LOCK，不如在每次执行 `/doc-harness` 指令时都重新确认身份。

这个建议非常聪明，因为：
1. doc-harness 的 5 个指令（init, check, sync, flush, recall）是 agent 最常执行的入口点
2. 每次执行时，agent 都会读取 skill 文件（SKILL.md → init.md/check.md/...）
3. 如果在这些 skill 指令中嵌入身份确认，agent 的 context 中会反复出现"我是 X 项目的代理"这一信息
4. 这比一次性读 CLAUDE.md 更有持续性防护效果

但这里有一个关键的技术问题：skill 文件本身不知道当前项目名称。SKILL.md 是通用的，不是项目特定的。当 agent 执行 `/doc-harness check` 时，它读取的是 `~/.claude/skills/doc-harness/check.md`，这个文件里没有项目名。

不过，agent 执行指令时已经知道自己在哪个目录、哪个项目。skill 文件可以要求 agent"在执行本指令前，确认你的项目身份"。

让我重新思考方案：

**方案 A（纯 CLAUDE.md）**：Identity lock 在 CLAUDE.md 顶部，读一次
**方案 B（纯 skill 指令）**：每次 doc-harness 指令执行时确认身份
**方案 C（混合）**：CLAUDE.md 有 lock + skill 指令每次确认

用户建议的是 B 或 C 的变体。

让我分析各种方案的优劣：

**方案 A 的问题**：
- 只读一次。如果 agent 之后 context 被大量其他项目信息占据，最初的 identity lock 可能被"覆盖"
- 但 agent 在 compact 后会重新读 CLAUDE.md，所以实际上会重新看到 lock

**方案 B 的问题**：
- skill 文件是通用的，不知道项目名
- 但 skill 可以要求"确认你当前所在的项目"
- 问题是：agent 只有在执行 doc-harness 指令时才会看到这些提示。如果 agent 连续工作几小时不触发 doc-harness 指令，中间发生漂移就挡不住

**方案 C（推荐）**：
- CLAUDE.md 顶部有 AGENT IDENTITY LOCK（长期锚定）
- 每次 doc-harness 指令执行时，skill 文件开头有一个身份确认仪式（短期强化）
- 两者互补

实际上，用户的建议让我想到了一个更优雅的方案：

**把身份确认嵌入 operational_rules.md 的每个工作节点**：

operational_rules.md 已经被嵌入到每个项目的 CLAUDE.md 中。但 operational_rules.md 是通用的。

更好的方案是：
1. CLAUDE.md 顶部有 AGENT IDENTITY LOCK（长期锚定）
2. skill 指令文件（check.md, sync.md, flush.md, init.md, recall.md）在执行流程的第一步加入身份确认
3. operational_rules.md 的 session start 流程加入 Step 0 身份确认

但 skill 文件是通用的，怎么知道项目名？

skill 文件可以这样写：
```
## 执行前身份确认

在读取本指令的剩余内容之前，先执行以下认知锚定：

> 🔒 **AGENT IDENTITY CHECK**
> 
> 确认：你当前所在的项目目录是 `[项目根目录]`。
> 确认：你是这个项目的代理，不是任何其他项目的代理。
> 如果以上任何一项不确定，立即停止并重新读取该项目的 CLAUDE.md。

---

## [后续指令内容]
```

这样每次执行 doc-harness 指令时，agent 都会看到这段文字。

但问题是：agent 读 skill 文件时，可能已经发生了认知漂移。如果 agent 把自己当成了 lit 的代理，它看到"确认你是这个项目的代理"时，可能会想"对，我是 lit 的代理"，然后继续错误操作。

所以 skill 文件里的确认需要更精确：不是"确认你是这个项目的代理"（太模糊），而是"确认你正在执行 doc-harness 指令的项目名称"。但 skill 文件不知道项目名称。

这是一个根本问题：通用 skill 文件无法绑定到具体项目。

除非... skill 文件要求 agent 在执行前做一件具体的事：
```
Step 0: 确认身份
- 查看当前工作目录
- 读取当前目录的 CLAUDE.md 第一行（项目名）
- 确认："我是 [项目名] 的代理"
```

这样 agent 就必须去读当前项目的 CLAUDE.md，而 CLAUDE.md 顶部有 AGENT IDENTITY LOCK。

这形成了一个**闭环**：
1. skill 指令要求"执行前先读当前目录的 CLAUDE.md 顶部，确认身份"
2. CLAUDE.md 顶部有 AGENT IDENTITY LOCK
3. agent 读到了锁，确认了身份
4. 然后执行 skill 指令

这比单纯在 CLAUDE.md 放锁更强，因为：
- 即使 agent 已经漂移，skill 指令会强制它重新读 CLAUDE.md
- 每次 doc-harness 操作都是一次"重新锚定"的机会

让我重新设计 plan，结合用户的建议：

**更新后的 v1.6.0 设计**：

1. **CLAUDE.md 顶部**：AGENT IDENTITY LOCK（长期锚定）
2. **每个 skill 指令文件开头**：强制身份确认仪式
   ```
   ## 执行前：身份确认（强制性）
   
   在继续阅读本指令之前，你必须：
   1. 查看当前工作目录，确认你在哪个项目
   2. 读取该项目的 CLAUDE.md 前 10 行（AGENT IDENTITY LOCK）
   3. 在内心确认："我是 [项目名] 的代理。我现在执行的是 doc-harness 指令。"
   
   如果身份不确定，立即停止并重新读取 CLAUDE.md。
   ---
   ```
3. **Recovery Chain Step 0**：session start 时确认身份
4. **operational_rules.md**：session start 和 session end 都加入身份确认
5. **Pre-send checklist**：跨项目发送时的 5 项自检
6. **check §1.11**：验证 identity lock 存在

这个设计的关键洞察是：**重复暴露 > 一次性暴露**。LLM 的 context 是动态的，身份认知需要不断被强化。

用户说"每次执行 doc-harness 的指令时，都确定一下自己属于哪个项目"。这个建议非常有价值，我应该采纳并把它融入方案。

让我给出回应，确认这个方向，并询问是否继续实施。

</details>

这是一个更深刻的洞察。**一次性锚定 vs. 重复强化**——对于 LLM 的动态 context 来说，后者更有效。

让我把两种机制结合起来：

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────┐
│  CLAUDE.md 顶部: AGENT IDENTITY LOCK    │  ← 长期锚定（到达时写死第一帧）
│  （你是谁 + 你不是谁）                   │
├─────────────────────────────────────────┤
│  每次 /doc-harness 指令执行时:           │  ← 重复强化（ skill 入口强制确认）
│  "先读当前目录 CLAUDE.md 前 10 行，      │
│   确认项目身份，再执行本指令"            │
├─────────────────────────────────────────┤
│  Recovery Chain Step 0:                │  ← 工作流内置（session start 仪式）
│  "确认身份 → 再读 must-read"             │
├─────────────────────────────────────────┤
│  跨项目发送 checklist:                   │  ← 操作前制动（5 项自检）
│  from 字段/outbox 路径/inbox 路径...    │
└─────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

**关键闭环**：skill 文件是通用的（不知道项目名），但它可以**强制 agent 去读当前项目的 CLAUDE.md 顶部**，而那里写着具体的项目名和 AGENT IDENTITY LOCK。即使 agent 已经漂移了，skill 指令的第一步会把它拉回来。

这样设计后，agent 在以下时刻都会重新确认身份：
- **到达项目时**（读 CLAUDE.md）
- **每次执行 doc-harness 指令时**（init/check/sync/flush/recall）
- **每个 session 开始时**（Recovery Chain Step 0）
- **向其他项目发信时**（pre-send checklist）

四个时间点形成**防御纵深**。

---

要不要我现在按这个**四层防御**模型实施 v1.6.0？

## Turn 6

### User

“你不是谁”不能要，并不是每个用户都有多个项目，并经常在项目之间写作。

### Assistant

<details><summary>Thinking</summary>

用户提出了一个重要修正："你不是谁"不能要。因为并不是每个用户都有多个项目，经常在项目之间工作。对于 standalone 项目来说，"你不是其他项目的代理"这句话是多余的，甚至可能让 agent 困惑（"其他项目？什么其他项目？"）。

这非常合理。让我重新思考 identity lock 的设计：

**核心修正**：
1. **不要"你不是谁"**——只声明"你是谁"
2. 跨项目边界（outbox/inbox 规则）放到 iron rules 里，不作为 identity 的一部分
3. Identity lock 是纯粹的**自我确认**，不是**边界警告**

**重新设计的 identity lock**：

基础版（所有项目）：
```
> 🔒 **AGENT IDENTITY LOCK**
>
> **你是 [PROJECT_NAME] 项目的代理。**
> 你的职责：[1-sentence].
>
> 如果你对自己的身份有任何怀疑，立即停止操作并重新读取本段落。
```

就这么简单。没有"你不是谁"，没有跨项目交互规则。

跨项目规则放到哪里？
- 放到 **Iron Rules** 里（作为行为规范）
- 放到 **operational_rules.md 的 inbox/outbox 部分**（作为操作流程）
- 放到 **Pre-send checklist** 里（作为操作前自检）

Identity lock 的职责就只有一个：**确认"我是谁"**。

用户说"并不是每个用户都有多个项目"。这进一步验证了：
- AGENT IDENTITY LOCK 应该是**所有项目**的标配
- 但内容应该是**最小化的**
- 跨项目相关的规则应该**分离**到 inbox/outbox 协议部分

让我给出回应，确认这个修正，然后询问是否开始实施。

</details>

正确。**Identity lock 的职责只有一个：确认"我是谁"。**

"你不是谁"把两个不同的问题混在一起了：
- **认知问题**（我是谁）→ identity lock
- **边界问题**（不要碰别人的东西）→ iron rules / inbox-outbox 协议

对于只有单个项目的用户，"你不是谁"不仅多余，还会制造困惑——agent 会浪费 token 去理解一个根本不存在的场景。

**修正后的设计**：

```
┌────────────────────────────────────────┐
│  CLAUDE.md 顶部（identity lock）        │
│                                        │
│  > 🔒 **AGENT IDENTITY LOCK**           │
│  >                                     │
│  > **你是 [PROJECT_NAME] 项目的代理。** │
│  > 你的职责：[一句话]。                 │
│  >                                     │
│  > 如果你对自己的身份有任何怀疑，       │
│  > 立即停止操作并重新读取本段落。       │
│                                        │
│  ← 只有"我是谁"，没有"我不是谁"       │
├────────────────────────────────────────┤
│  Iron Rules（行为规范）                 │
│                                        │
│  - 项目间通讯走 inbox/outbox（如有）    │
│  - 不修改其他项目内部文档               │
│  - from 字段写本项目名                  │
│                                        │
│  ← 边界规则放在这里，按需配置           │
└────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

**skill 指令里的身份确认**也简化为：
> "执行本指令前，先读当前目录 CLAUDE.md 的 AGENT IDENTITY LOCK，确认：你是 [项目名] 的代理。"

没有"你不是其他项目的代理"这句。

---

四层防御模型更新：

| 层级 | 时机 | 内容 | 是否通用 |
|------|------|------|----------|
| 1. 长期锚定 | 读 CLAUDE.md | "你是 X 的代理" | ✅ 所有项目 |
| 2. 重复强化 | 每次 doc-harness 指令 | 强制读 identity lock | ✅ 所有项目 |
| 3. 工作流仪式 | session start | Step 0 确认身份 | ✅ 所有项目 |
| 4. 操作前制动 | 跨项目发送时 | Pre-send checklist | 仅 inbox/outbox 项目 |

等等，我需要保持结构清晰。让我重新考虑。

在 WhoAMI 的实现中，AGENT IDENTITY LOCK 是在标题之后、所有其他内容之前。用 `>` blockquote。

但 spec 的模板是用 `---` 分隔的。让我看看现有模板结构：

```
# [PROJECT_NAME] — Entry Document

**Last updated**: YYYY-MM-DD

**One-line status (as of YYYY-MM-DD)**: [Brief description]

```

我需要在标题后、元数据前插入 identity lock。让我这样设计：

```
# [PROJECT_NAME] — Entry Document

> 🔒 **AGENT IDENTITY LOCK**
>
> **你是 [PROJECT_NAME] 项目的代理。**
> [One-sentence role description.]
>
> 如果你对自己的身份有任何怀疑，立即停止操作并重新读取本段落。

---

**Last updated**: YYYY-MM-DD
```

这样结构清晰：标题 → identity lock → 分隔线 → 元数据 → Recovery Chain...

### 2. §11.1 Session Start

当前：
```
Follow the project's Recovery Chain (defined in CLAUDE.md §Recovery Chain):

1. Read the **must-read** layer in order (CLAUDE.md → CURRENT_STATUS.md, typically 2–3 files).
2. Scan the **task-conditional** layer. Read only the entries whose condition matches the current work.
3. If user is present → confirm whether next steps have changed.
4. If compact recovery (user not present) → continue per headlights.
```

```
Follow the project's Recovery Chain (defined in CLAUDE.md §Recovery Chain):

**Step 0 — Identity anchor** (before reading any files):
```

```json
{
  "todos": [
    {
      "title": "Phase 1: skill/spec.md + skill-zh/spec.md",
      "status": "in_progress"
```

    97	### 2.3 Template
    98	
    99	CLAUDE.md consists of three parts: project-specific information + embedded operational rules + pointer to full spec.
   100	
   101	```markdown
   102	# [PROJECT_NAME] — Entry Document
   103	
   104	**Last updated**: YYYY-MM-DD
   105	**Current phase**: [Phase name] (⏳/⏸️/✅)
   106	**One-line status (as of YYYY-MM-DD)**: [Brief description]
   107	
   108	---
   109	
   110	## Recovery Chain
   111	
   112	Recovery Chain is the entry ritual for any agent or human resuming work on this project.
   113	It has two layers.
   114	
   115	### Must-read (baseline)
   116	
   117	Files any continuation must read. Keep to 2–3 entries.
   118	
   119	1. This file (CLAUDE.md)
   120	2. `CURRENT_STATUS.md`
   121	
   122	### Task-conditional
   123	
   124	Read only if the work matches. Grows and shrinks as the project evolves.
   125	
   126	- If looking up a specific file: read `FILE_INDEX.md`
   127	- If investigating historical phase details: read `WORKLOG.md`
   128	- [Add project-specific entries as needed — e.g., "If doing X: read Y.md"]
   129	
   130	### Meta-rules
   131	
   132	- Recovery Chain is **self-contained**: every entry points to a file inside the project
   133	  (or a stable sibling-project path). Do not depend on agent-side features
   134	  (memory systems, chat history, external services) — those may not exist for the next agent.
   135	- Recovery Chain is **living**: add entries when new classes of work appear; remove entries
   136	  when work categories retire. Review at phase transitions.
   137	
   138	## Project Overview
   139	
   140	[3-5 lines: project goals, outputs, key context]
   141	
   142	## Project-Level Iron Rules
   143	
   144	[Permanently valid, phase-independent rules]
   145	- Iron rule 1: ...
   146	- Iron rule 2: ...
   147	
   148	## Key Technical Information
   149	
   150	[Stable technical details: build commands, path conventions, dependencies]
   151	
   152	## Sub-projects (if any)
   153	
   154	- `subproject/` → see [subproject/CLAUDE.md](subproject/CLAUDE.md) (status: ⏳/⏸️/✅)
   155	
   156	## Doc Harness — Operational Rules
   157	
   158	[EMBED FULL CONTENT OF operational_rules.md HERE (~106 lines).
   159	 These rules are the complete guide for daily status document maintenance.
   160	 For full design rationale, see DOC_HARNESS_SPEC.md in project root.]
   161	```

   713	## Chapter 11: Agent Behavior Guidelines
   714	
   715	### 11.1 Session Start — Applying Recovery Chain
   716	
   717	Follow the project's Recovery Chain (defined in CLAUDE.md §Recovery Chain):
   718	
   719	1. Read the **must-read** layer in order (CLAUDE.md → CURRENT_STATUS.md, typically 2–3 files).
   720	2. Scan the **task-conditional** layer. Read only the entries whose condition matches the current work.
   721	3. If user is present → confirm whether next steps have changed.
   722	4. If compact recovery (user not present) → continue per headlights.
   723	
   724	Do not unconditionally read all task-conditional entries at startup. That defeats the purpose of the two-layer split. If you find yourself reading a file every session, it probably belongs in must-read — promote it explicitly.
   725	
   726	### 11.2 During Work
   727	
   728	1. Complete a **meaningful step** → update CURRENT_STATUS car body
   729	2. Create a new file → **do two things simultaneously**: (1) register in FILE_INDEX (2) record in CURRENT_STATUS car body
   730	3. **"Write It Down"**: important analysis results, design ideas, decision rationale → save to file + register
   731	4. **Watch remaining context** (if exposed by the runtime): context compression is involuntary session end. If your environment reports a context-usage percentage or token count, treat **low remaining context** (~<20%) as an immediate trigger — update CURRENT_STATUS before the next tool call; if the car body has **substantial unsaved work**, consider a phase transition now. Don't wait for a "meaningful step" that may never land.
   732	
   733	   **"Substantial unsaved work" — concrete threshold** (any one suffices): (a) ≥3 completed `####` step headings since the last car-body flush; (b) ≥50 lines added to the car body since the last flush; (c) car body ≥100 lines (half the 200-line phase-transition threshold). If none of (a)–(c) apply, just flush — don't force a phase transition from a thin car body.
   734	
   735	### 11.3 Session End
   736	
   737	1. Ensure CURRENT_STATUS car body reflects all work from this session
   738	2. Update headlights "next steps"
   739	3. Update CURRENT_STATUS "last updated" date
   740	4. Update CLAUDE.md "one-line status (as of date)"
   741	5. Check: are all files created this session registered in FILE_INDEX?
   742	6. Check: is there any important information only in context? → Write it down!


</details>

   960	**Body**: free-form Markdown. Tables, checklists, code blocks permitted.
   961	
   962	### 14.3.1 Pre-send verification (sender's responsibility)
   963	
   964	Before writing a new message to a recipient's `inbox/`, the sender **must** verify that the recipient has the inbox/outbox protocol active. Otherwise delivery is silent-failure: a file lands in a directory the recipient never scans, or the copy fails with `ENOENT` on a nonexistent target.
   965	
   966	Verification steps (in order, stop at first failure):
   967	1. **Target path exists**: the recipient project directory exists and is reachable from the sender.
   968	2. **Recipient's `inbox/` exists**: if absent, the recipient has not adopted the protocol (or is no longer participating). **Do not create `inbox/` in the recipient's project** — that would silently opt them in without consent.
   969	3. **Recipient's CLAUDE.md contains the inter-project iron rule block** (grep for the string `inbox/` in recipient CLAUDE.md). This confirms the recipient's next agent will actually scan its inbox.
   970	
   971	**If any step fails**: do NOT copy the file to recipient's `inbox/`. Instead:
   972	- Write the message to your own `outbox/` as normal (permanent record).
   973	- Record the failed delivery in CURRENT_STATUS car body: `#### Attempted to send <topic> to <recipient> on YYYY-MM-DD — recipient has not adopted inbox/outbox protocol. Message held in own outbox only.`
   974	- Raise the issue with the user at the next opportunity. Do not retry automatically.
   975	
   976	### 14.4 Message lifecycle and rules
   977	
   978	```
   979	Sender                                        Recipient
   980	  │                                              │
   981	  ├─ writes new message to own outbox/           │
   982	  ├─ copies the same file into recipient inbox/  │
   983	  │  (status: unread, set by sender)             │
   984	  │                                              │
   985	  │   ─── session boundary ───                   │
   986	  │                                              │
   987	  │                      recipient's Recovery ──┤
   988	  │                      Chain points to inbox/ ─┤
   989	  │                      recipient reads msg    ─┤
   990	  │                      → status: read         ─┤
   991	  │                      performs any action    ─┤
   992	  │                      → status: actioned     ─┤
   993	  │                      (if reply needed:      ─┤
   994	  │                       sends a NEW message)  ─┤
   995	```
   996	
   997	**Rules**:
   998	
   999	1. **Received messages are immutable** — never edit a file in your `inbox/` beyond updating the `status` field. To respond, write a new message.
  1000	2. **Status transitions** — sender sets `unread` at delivery. Recipient changes to `read` after reading, then to `actioned` after completing any required action. An `actioned` message with no required action is equivalent to acknowledged-and-closed.
  1001	3. **Archival** — messages older than 30 days with `status: actioned` **should** be moved to `inbox/_archive/` (same structure inside). The archival audit runs as part of `/doc-harness check` §1.7 — when the check finds ≥5 actioned messages older than 30 days, it flags archival as an action item; the agent performs the move during the same session. Archived messages are permanent records; do not delete.
  1002	4. **Sender retains a copy** — the sender's `outbox/` is the permanent draft/record. If the recipient loses their copy, the sender's `outbox/` is authoritative for what was sent.
  1003	5. **Cross-project reference snapshots** — when communicating numbers, deliverables, or state ("our model reached accuracy 0.88"), send a **snapshot** in an inbox message rather than pointing the recipient at your internal files. Internal files churn and refactors break external references. A snapshot, once delivered, does not lie.
  1004	
  1005	### 14.5 Integration with the four core documents
  1006	
  1007	**CLAUDE.md** — add one iron rule block (copy-paste template, no customization required):
  1008	
  1009	```markdown
  1010	**Inter-project communication via inbox/outbox (file-based protocol)**
  1011	
  1012	- **Mechanism**: This project maintains `inbox/` (received messages) and `outbox/` (sent messages). Messages are Markdown files with YAML frontmatter; filename `YYYY-MM-DD-from-<source>-<topic>.md`.
  1013	- **Why this is mandatory (if adopted)**: Cross-project information exchanged only in chat is lost on session end. File-based messages survive session boundaries and are discoverable by any future agent through this project's Recovery Chain.
  1014	- **Receiving**: Recovery Chain checks `inbox/` for `status: unread`. Read → update to `status: read`. After acting on the message → `status: actioned`. Never edit received messages beyond the status field; to respond, write a new message.
  1015	- **Sending**: Write to this project's `outbox/` (permanent sender-side record) AND copy the same file into the recipient project's `inbox/`. Record the exchange in CURRENT_STATUS so it is traceable next session.
  1016	- **Snapshots over pointers**: When communicating numbers/deliverables to another project, put the value in the message body rather than referencing internal files.
  1017	- **Full specification**: `DOC_HARNESS_SPEC.md` §14 (in this project's root).
  1018	```
  1019	
  1020	**CURRENT_STATUS.md** — when an incoming message requires action, add it to Headlights:
  1021	
  1022	```markdown
  1023	### Immediate Actions
  1024	- [ ] Respond to <sender>'s <topic> (see `inbox/YYYY-MM-DD-from-<source>-<topic>.md`)
  1025	```
  1026	
  1027	Also record outbound exchanges in the car body as they happen:
  1028	
  1029	```markdown
  1030	#### Sent deliverable to <target> (YYYY-MM-DD)
  1031	- Message: `outbox/YYYY-MM-DD-from-<this-project>-<topic>.md` (same filename convention as §14.3 — the outbox file has the same name as the copy sent to the recipient's inbox)
  1032	- Summary: <one line>
  1033	```
  1034	
  1035	**FILE_INDEX.md** — register both directories under their own category:
  1036	
  1037	```markdown
  1038	## Inter-Project Communication
  1039	- `inbox/` — Incoming messages from other projects


</details>

  1070	3. Add the task-conditional entry to Recovery Chain (also §14.5).
  1071	4. Add the `## Inter-Project Communication` category to FILE_INDEX.
  1072	5. (Optional) Send a notification message to dependent projects that this project is now reachable via inbox.
  1073	
  1074	### 14.8 Malformed message handling
  1075	
  1076	When `inbox/` contains a file that does not conform to §14.3, do NOT silently skip it and do NOT guess. Apply the classification below, then act once — never enter a retry loop on a malformed file.
  1077	
  1078	| Symptom | Lenient or strict? | Action |
  1079	|---------|--------------------|--------|
  1080	| Filename does not match `YYYY-MM-DD-from-<source>-<topic>.md` but file has valid YAML | Lenient | Process normally. Note the filename anomaly in CURRENT_STATUS car body. Do NOT rename the file (it's the sender's record, immutable per §14.4 rule 1). |
  1081	| No YAML frontmatter at all | Strict | Move to `inbox/_malformed/` (create if missing). Write a one-line entry in CURRENT_STATUS car body: `#### Quarantined malformed inbox/<filename> (no YAML) on YYYY-MM-DD`. Do NOT attempt to parse the body. |
  1082	| YAML frontmatter present but `status:` field missing | Strict | Treat as `unread` for safety (err toward action). Add the `status: unread` line and proceed to read. Log the anomaly in car body. |
  1083	| `status:` has unknown value (not `unread`/`read`/`actioned`) | Strict | Treat as `unread`. Log the anomaly in car body. After reading, set to `read` (then `actioned` if applicable) using canonical values. |
  1084	| Required frontmatter field missing (`from`, `to`, `date`, `subject`) | Strict | Move to `inbox/_malformed/` with a one-line car body note. Do NOT fabricate the missing values. All four are required per §14.3. |
  1085	| `priority:` missing or has unknown value | Lenient | Treat as `priority: normal`. Log the anomaly in car body. |
  1086	| `in-reply-to:` missing entirely | Lenient | Treat as no-reply (null). No action needed. |
  1087	| Frontmatter references `in-reply-to:` pointing at a file that does not exist in this project's outbox | Lenient | Process normally; note the dangling reference in car body but do not block. |
  1088	| Multiple messages with the same filename (rare even after §14.3 disambiguator, e.g. two senders writing independently at the same moment) | Strict | The one on disk wins. Note in car body: `#### Filename collision observed on <name> — kept disk copy`. Do not merge contents. Report via `/doc-harness check` §1.7 so the sender can re-send with a different topic slug if needed. |
  1089	
  1090	`inbox/_malformed/` is not archival — it's a quarantine for agent/human inspection. Entries there should be reviewed by the user, not silently forgotten. `/doc-harness check` §1.7 reports the count.
  1091

  1097	|--------|------------|
  1098	| Work goal fundamentally changes ("writing" → "reviewing") | ✅ Yes |
  1099	| User explicitly says "start something else" | ✅ Yes |

  1371	
  1372	## Appendix E: Design Choices (FAQ)
  1373	
  1374	### Why is inter-project inbox/outbox an optional mechanism, not a required one?
  1375	
  1376	Because many projects are standalone and have no dependents. Mandating inbox/outbox on every project would impose empty directories and an unused iron rule, eroding trust in the skill. The mechanism is offered as a standard optional feature with a complete self-contained spec (Chapter 14) so projects that need it can adopt it consistently and projects that don't need it ignore it.
  1377	
  1378	### Why is the mechanism described inside doc-harness instead of as a separate spec?
  1379	


</details>

  1120	
  1121	## Appendix C: Glossary
  1122	
  1123	| Term | Definition |
  1124	|------|-----------|
  1125	| **Project** | Basic unit of the Doc Harness system. A work stream with independent goals and outputs. |
  1126	| **Phase** | A period within a project with a clear goal. Transition triggers information flow operations. |
  1127	| **Leaf document** | Any file that is not one of the four core status documents. |
  1128	| **Car body / Tire tracks / Headlights / Driving manual** | Metaphors for the four sections of CURRENT_STATUS. |
  1129	| **Register** | Add a file to the appropriate category in FILE_INDEX. |
  1130	| **Write It Down** | First principle: important information must be saved to file and registered. |
  1131	| **SUPERSEDED** | Document has been replaced; marked at first line. |
  1132	| **Iron rule** | Project-level permanent rule defined in CLAUDE.md. |
  1133	
  1134	---
  1135	
  1136	## Appendix D: Worked Example — Four Documents Through Two Phase Transitions
  1137	
  1138	Using a hypothetical research paper project to show how all four documents evolve from project start through Phase 3.
  1139	
  1140	### Project Start (Phase 1 begins)
  1141	
  1142	**CLAUDE.md**:
  1143	```
  1144	# Market Microstructure Paper — Entry Document
  1145	Last updated: 2026-03-01
  1146	Current phase: Model Building (⏳)
  1147	One-line status (as of 2026-03-01): Project just started, building base model
  1148	
  1149	## Recovery Chain


</details>

<details><summary>Tool Result: ReadFile (`skill/spec.md`)</summary>

<!-- call_id: tool_x69EConB3K6hxKfTSbzULSaU -->
<system>21 lines read from file starting from line 1388. Total lines in file: 1408. End of file reached. Lines [1405] were truncated.</system>
  1388	Any larger, and "must-read" becomes "should probably read," and agents start skipping entries or reading the whole project defensively. The two-layer split only works if the baseline is genuinely minimal. Entries that only apply to *some* work belong in task-conditional.
  1389	
  1390	### Why use line count (not phase count) as WORKLOG archival trigger?
  1391	
  1392	Phase density varies enormously across projects — from ~20 lines per phase (infrastructure work, terse records) to ~200 lines per phase (dense research work). Line count reflects the actual cost of reading the file, which is what we care about.
  1393

operational_rules.md archival section catches up to spec §5.5. **Structural (skill-creator review)**: SKILL.md description rewritten for triggering...
  1406	| v1.3 | 2026-04-19 | New Chapter 14: Optional Inter-Project Communication (inbox/outbox) — self-contained, portable mechanism for file-based cross-project messaging. Spec covers folder structure, message format (YAML frontmatter + Markdown body), lifecycle (unread→read→actioned), integration with all four core documents, quick start for fresh agents, and adopt-on-existing-project procedure. init gains one y/n prompt to enable. Appendix E updated to explain why the mechanism is optional and why it lives inside doc-harness rather than as an external spec. "Portfolio" framing removed throughout — project groups are flat peers. §11.2 gains a context-aware update rule: if the runtime exposes context-window usage, low remaining context (~<20%) is an immediate trigger to flush CURRENT_STATUS and possibly phase-transition. |
  1407	| v1.4.1 | 2026-04-19 | **§5.5 WORKLOG archival correction — field feedback**: archive filename changed from quarterly bin `WORKLOG_ARCHIVE_<YYYY-QN>.md` to per-event date `WORKLOG_ARCHIVE_<YYYY-MM-DD>.md`. The quarterly scheme unbounded the archive for high-activity projects (a project writing 5,000 lines/quarter would put all 5,000 lines into one "archive" file, defeating the purpose). Per-event naming keeps each archive inherently bounded by the ~1000-line trigger. Cross-quarter-scar step (old rule 6) removed — no longer applicable. New rule 7: archival event must be recorded in CURRENT_STATUS car body so a next-session agent sees the history shift without diffing WORKLOG. Git commit message updated to `Archive WORKLOG <YYYY-MM-DD>`. Operational_rules.md mirror-updated. TOC chapter-5 description adjusted. |
  1408	| v1.5.0 | 2026-04-22 | **Two new commands**: `/doc-harness sync` (status synchronization — drift repair, date refresh, file registration, optional phase transition/archival; auto/interactive modes) and `/doc-harness flush` (emergency context save — includes sync plus mandatory context-to-document extraction with inventory, heuristic classification, verification, and flush marker; auto/interactive modes). New reference documents `sync.md` and `flush.md`. Spec gains §11.5 (sync) and §11.6 (flush). Operational rules updated to reference both commands.   1094	## Appendix A: Phase Boundary Decision Guide
  1095	
  1096	| Signal | Transition? |
  1097	|--------|------------|
  1098	| Work goal fundamentally changes ("writing" → "reviewing") | ✅ Yes |
  1099	| User explicitly says "start something else" | ✅ Yes |
  1100	| Project pause >3 days | ✅ Yes (pause = phase end) |
  1101	| Car body exceeds 200 lines | ✅ Consider (signal, not hard rule) |
  1102	| Sub-task switch within same goal (Ch4→Ch5, both "literature reinforcement") | ❌ No — use sub-headings in car body |
  1103	| Temporary small task (fix a typo, then return) | ❌ No |
  1104	| Uncertain | ❌ Don't transition (avoid over-maintenance); use clear headings in car body |

     1	# Doc Harness — Operational Rules
     2	
     3	<!-- doc-harness-ops-start -->
     4	<!-- doc-harness-ops-version: 1.5.1 -->
     5	
     6	> This section is embedded in each project's CLAUDE.md as the complete guide for maintaining status documents.
     7	> For full design rationale, see `DOC_HARNESS_SPEC.md` (in the project root directory).
     8	> The HTML comments `doc-harness-ops-start` / `doc-harness-ops-end` delimit the embedded region — `init.md` re-embed and `/doc-harness check` §1.10 use them to locate and replace the block safely. Do not remove either marker. The `doc-harness-ops-version: N.N` tag is read by `check.md` §1.10 to detect stale operational-rules sections after a skill upgrade.
     9	
    10	---
    11	
    12	## First Principle: "Write It Down or Lose It"
    13	
    14	All information in context will eventually be lost completely. Important information must be **written to a file** and **registered in FILE_INDEX**. Not written = lost. Not registered = exists but undiscoverable = effectively lost. Better to write one extra file than to let information exist only in context.
    15	
    16	## Four Core Documents
    17	
    18	| Document | Role | When to update |
    19	|----------|------|---------------|
    20	| **CLAUDE.md** | Project entry. Overview, recovery chain, iron rules, these operational rules | Phase transitions for body; "one-line status" refreshed every session end |


</details>

<!-- call_id: tool_GdTL3F2aMq3Zf9T2ufUmcUlw -->
<system>50 lines read from file starting from line 90. Total lines in file: 189.</system>
    90	
    91	## Recovery Chain (Session Start)
    92	
    93	Recovery Chain is defined in CLAUDE.md and has two layers:
    94	
    95	**Must-read** (2–3 files, baseline for any continuation):
    96	1. CLAUDE.md (project scope, iron rules, operational rules)
    97	2. CURRENT_STATUS.md (tire tracks / car body / headlights / driving manual)
    98	
    99	**Task-conditional** (read only if the work matches):
   100	- If looking up a file: read FILE_INDEX.md
   101	- If investigating phase history: read WORKLOG.md
   102	- [Project-specific entries added over time]
   103	
   104	**Meta-rules**:
   105	- Recovery Chain is **self-contained**: only project-internal files (or stable sibling-project paths). No dependency on agent-side features (memory, chat history, external services) — those may not exist for the next agent.
   106	- Recovery Chain is **living**: update it at phase transitions (add entries for new work classes; remove retired ones).
   107	
   108	**Applying at session start**:
   109	1. Read must-read layer in order.
   110	2. Scan task-conditional; read only entries whose condition matches current work.
   111	3. If user present → confirm whether next steps have changed. Compact recovery without user → continue per headlights.
   112	
   113	## During Work
   114	
   115	- Complete a **meaningful step** → update CURRENT_STATUS car body. "Meaningful" = if context is lost now, next agent needs to know this step is done.
   116	- Create a new file → **do two things simultaneously**: (1) register in FILE_INDEX (2) record in CURRENT_STATUS car body.
   117	- Important information → **immediately** write to file and register (Write It Down!).
   118	- **Watch remaining context** (if the runtime exposes it). Compression is involuntary session end. When remaining context drops low (~<20%), update CURRENT_STATUS *before* the next tool call; if the car body holds substantial unsaved work, consider a phase transition now. Don't wait for the next "meaningful step" — it may not land in time. If the user notices context is running low, they may request `/doc-harness flush` to systematically save all important context information to files before compression.
   119	
   120	## Session End Checklist
   121	
   122	- [ ] CURRENT_STATUS car body reflects all work from this session?
   123	- [ ] Headlights "next steps" are accurate?
   124	- [ ] CURRENT_STATUS "last updated" date refreshed?
   125	- [ ] CLAUDE.md "one-line status (as of date)" refreshed?
   126	- [ ] All files created this session registered in FILE_INDEX?
   127	- [ ] Any important information only in context? → Write it down!
   128	- [ ] If a phase transition occurred: WORKLOG under ~1000 lines? (Over → trigger archival.)
   129	
   130	> The user may request `/doc-harness check` at any time for a comprehensive health audit and principle reflection. Recommended to run as a background agent to avoid interrupting current work.
   131	> If significant drift is detected (files unregistered, dates stale, car body over limit), the user may request `/doc-harness sync` to repair it automatically.
   132	> If context compression is imminent, run `/doc-harness flush` to systematically extract all important context information into documents before it is lost.
   133	
   134	## Status Sync and Context Flush
   135	
   136	Two commands complement the daily workflow:
   137	
   138	- **`/doc-harness sync`** — Repair documentation drift. Scans for unregistered files, stale dates, and length thresholds; executes fixes; optionally triggers phase transition or WORKLOG archival. Auto mode (default) executes without asking; interactive mode asks before major changes.
   139	- **`/doc-harness flush`** — Emergency save. Includes everything `sync` does, plus mandatory extraction of important context information into documents. Use when context is about to compress or reset. After a successful flush, a new agent reading the Recovery Chain should recover state as if context had never been compressed.


</details>

   165	- **`PHILOSOPHY.md`** — Principles from practice: generalizable lessons forged by this project's specific work. Each entry: principle statement, the practice that forged it, scope, first-recorded date. Principles may be shared into sibling projects' PHILOSOPHY.md; this file remains the birthplace record for *this* project. Use when an insight likely applies beyond the immediate situation.
   166

   168	
   169	## Optional Inter-Project Communication (inbox/outbox)
   170	
   171	Adopted when this project coordinates with other projects (dependencies in either direction, repeated cross-project decisions/deliverables). If `inbox/` and `outbox/` directories exist at the project root, the protocol is active.
   172	
   173	**Receiving**:
   174	- Recovery Chain task-conditional includes: "If `inbox/` has any file with `status: unread`: read them."
   175	- Read the message → update its YAML `status` field to `read` → perform any required action → update to `actioned`.
   176	- Never edit received messages beyond the status field. To respond, write a **new** message.
   177	
   178	**Sending**:
   179	- Filename: `YYYY-MM-DD-from-<this-project>-<topic-slug>.md`.
   180	- YAML frontmatter: `from`, `to`, `date`, `subject`, `status: unread` (sender sets), `in-reply-to` (if reply), `priority`.
   181	- Body: free-form Markdown.
   182	- Write to this project's `outbox/` (sender-side permanent record) AND copy the same file to recipient's `inbox/`.
   183	- Record the exchange in CURRENT_STATUS car body.
   184	
   185	**Snapshots over pointers**: when communicating numbers/deliverables to another project, put the value in the message body — do NOT point the recipient at your internal files (they churn and break external references).
   186	
   187	Complete specification, including archival (30-day actioned messages → `inbox/_archive/`) and retrofit procedure: see `DOC_HARNESS_SPEC.md` Chapter 14.

   180	
   181	If the user opted in (see Step 1), do the following:
   182	
   183	**(a) Create folders**: `inbox/` and `outbox/` at project root (both empty; git-track with `.gitkeep` if needed).
   184	
   185	**(b) Add the iron rule block** to CLAUDE.md inside the Iron Rules section (copy-paste, no customization needed):
   186	
   187	```markdown
   188	**Inter-project communication via inbox/outbox (file-based protocol)**
   189	
   190	- **Mechanism**: This project maintains `inbox/` (received messages) and `outbox/` (sent messages). Messages are Markdown files with YAML frontmatter; filename `YYYY-MM-DD-from-<source>-<topic>.md`.
   191	- **Why this is mandatory (if adopted)**: Cross-project information exchanged only in chat is lost on session end. File-based messages survive session boundaries and are discoverable by any future agent through this project's Recovery Chain.
   192	- **Receiving**: Recovery Chain checks `inbox/` for `status: unread`. Read → update to `status: read`. After acting on the message → `status: actioned`. Never edit received messages beyond the status field; to respond, write a new message.
   193	- **Sending**: Write to this project's `outbox/` (permanent sender-side record) AND copy the same file into the recipient project's `inbox/`. Record the exchange in CURRENT_STATUS so it is traceable next session.
   194	- **Snapshots over pointers**: When communicating numbers/deliverables to another project, put the value in the message body rather than referencing internal files.
   195	- **Full specification**: `DOC_HARNESS_SPEC.md` §14 (in this project's root).
   196	```
   197	
   198	**(c) Add to Recovery Chain** task-conditional layer in CLAUDE.md:
   199	
   200	```markdown
   201	- If `inbox/` has any file with `status: unread`: read and action those first
   202	```
   203	
   204	**(d) Register in FILE_INDEX**:
   205	
   206	```markdown
   207	## Inter-Project Communication
   208	- `inbox/` — Incoming messages from other projects
   209	- `outbox/` — Outgoing messages (drafts and sent-copies)
   210	```

   233	## Language-independence note
   234	
   235	All Part-1 anchors (`## Current Work`, `## Recent Completed`, `## Next Steps`, `## Current Working Principles`, `Iron Rules`, `Driving Manual`, etc.) match **either English or Chinese** headings produced by `init.md` templates — implementations should Grep for either variant. A mixed-language project (e.g., Chinese CLAUDE.md but English CURRENT_STATUS) still checks correctly as long as each document uses one consistent language internally.

   263	📝 Write It Down: [status]

   268	[specific fixes for ❌/⚠️ items]

   145	
   146	Grep for the HTML comment `<!-- doc-harness-ops-version: N.N -->` anywhere in CLAUDE.md (case-insensitive, one line).
   147	- Found and matches the version of the installed skill (e.g. `1.4`) → `✅ Operational rules up to date (vN.N)`
   148	- Found but older than installed skill → `⚠️ Operational rules snapshot is vX.X; installed skill is vY.Y — re-embed from operational_rules.md to upgrade`
   149	- Missing entirely → `⚠️ No version marker found — this CLAUDE.md predates v1.4 or was hand-edited. Recommend re-embedding operational_rules.md.`
   150	
   151	The installed skill's version is the `**Version**` line at the top of the installed `spec.md`. **Resolve the install path in this order** (first hit wins):
   152	
   153	1. Project-level: `<project_root>/.claude/skills/doc-harness/spec.md`
   154	2. User-level, Claude Code default on Unix: `$HOME/.claude/skills/doc-harness/spec.md`
   155	3. User-level, XDG override: `${XDG_CONFIG_HOME:-$HOME/.config}/claude/skills/doc-harness/spec.md`
   156	4. User-level, Windows: `%USERPROFILE%\.claude\skills\doc-harness\spec.md` (bash: `"$USERPROFILE/.claude/skills/doc-harness/spec.md"` — forward slashes work on Windows bash)

     1	# 状态文档体系规范（Status Documentation System Specification）
     2

42----
43-
44-## 第一章 首要原则与概述
45-
46-### 1.1 首要原则："落笔为安"（Write It Down or Lose It）
47-
48-Context中的一切信息都是临时的。无论多重要的分析结果、多精妙的设计思路，只要没有**写入文件**并**注册到FILE_INDEX**，就等于不存在。
--
708:## 第十一章 Agent行为规范
709-
710-### 11.1 Session开始——应用恢复链
711-
712-按项目 CLAUDE.md 中定义的恢复链执行：
713-
714-1. 按顺序读**必读**层（CLAUDE.md → CURRENT_STATUS.md，通常 2–3 个文件）。
715-2. 扫描**任务条件读**层。只读条件匹配当前工作的条目。
716-3. 如果用户在场 → 确认"下一步"是否仍然正确。
717-4. 如果是 compact 恢复（用户不在场）→ 直接按车灯继续。
718-
719-不要在启动时无条件读完所有任务条件读条目——那会让两层切分失去意义。如果你发现某条条件读条目每次都读，它其实属于必读层，应显式提升。
720-
721-### 11.2 工作过程中
722-
723-1. 每完成一个**有意义的步骤** → 更新CURRENT_STATUS车身
724-2. 创建新文件 → **同时做两件事**：(1)注册FILE_INDEX (2)记录在CURRENT_STATUS车身
725-3. **"落笔为安"**：重要分析结果、设计思路、决策理由 → 写入文件 + 注册
726-4. **关注剩余 context**（如运行环境暴露该信息）：context 压缩等同于非自愿的 session 结束。如果环境报告 context 使用率（百分比或 token 数），将**剩余不足**（~<20%）视为立即触发——在下一次工具调用前更新 CURRENT_STATUS；如果车身已积累**大量未保存的工作**，立即考虑阶段切换。别等那个可能永远不会到来的"有意义的步骤"。
727-
728-   **"大量未保存的工作"——具体阈值**（任一成立即可）：(a) 距上次车身刷新已完成 ≥3 个 `####` 步骤；(b) 距上次刷新车身已新增 ≥50 行；(c) 车身已 ≥100 行（阶段切换 200 行阈值的一半）。若 (a)–(c) 均不成立，只刷新即可——不必从单薄的车身强行触发阶段切换。

</details>

<details><summary>Tool Result: Grep (`skill-zh/spec.md`)</summary>

<!-- call_id: tool_jnPhvU4sDueN4361jhea23kJ -->
957:### 14.3.1 发送前验证（发送方责任）
958-
959-在向接收方 `inbox/` 写入新消息前，发送方**必须**先验证接收方已启用 inbox/outbox 协议，否则会造成静默失败：文件落入接收方从不扫描的目录，或因目标不存在而 `ENOENT` 失败。
960-
961-验证步骤（按顺序；命中任一失败即停止）：
962-1. **目标路径存在**：接收方项目目录存在且发送方可访问。
963-2. **接收方 `inbox/` 存在**：若无，则接收方尚未采用协议（或已不再参与）。**不要替接收方创建 `inbox/` 目录**——那相当于未经许可地为其开启协议。
964-3. **接收方 CLAUDE.md 含有 inbox/outbox 铁律块**（对接收方 CLAUDE.md Grep 字符串 `inbox/`），这确认接收方的下一个 agent 确实会扫描 inbox。
965-
966-**任何一步失败**：**不要**把文件复制到接收方 `inbox/`。改为：
967-- 按常规写入自己 `outbox/`（作为永久记录）。
968-- 在 CURRENT_STATUS 车身记录送达失败：`#### 尝试向 <接收方> 发送 <主题>（YYYY-MM-DD）——接收方未采用 inbox/outbox 协议，消息仅存于自己 outbox。`
969-- 下次与用户交互时提出。**不要**自动重试。
970-
971-### 14.4 消息生命周期与规则
972-
--

44-## 第一章 首要原则与概述
--
61:| **CLAUDE.md** | 门牌 | 项目入口、恢复起点、项目级铁律 | 阶段切换时 |
62-| **CURRENT_STATUS.md** | 行驶中的汽车 | 当前阶段活跃信息、近期历史摘要、下一步、阶段级原则 | 每个session |
63-| **FILE_INDEX.md** | 图书馆目录 | 按类别索引项目所有文件 | 文件变化时 |
64:| **WORKLOG.md** | 行车记录仪 | 永久保存所有阶段的完整工作详情 | 阶段切换时（批量） |
65-

   135

   137	
   138	- **`/doc-harness sync`** — 修复文档漂移。扫描未注册文件、陈旧日期和长度阈值；执行修复；可选触发阶段切换或 WORKLOG 归档。交互模式（默认）在重大变更前询问；自动模式无需询问即执行。
   139	- **`/doc-harness flush`** — 紧急保存。包含 `sync` 的一切功能，加上强制性上下文信息提取到文档。用于上下文即将压缩或重置时。成功冲刷后，全新智能体阅读恢复链应能恢复到仿佛上下文从未被压缩的状态。

    71	- 恢复链是**活的**：阶段切换时审查并更新。

     1	---
     2	name: doc-harness

Use this skill whenever the user wants to structure a long-running project, track progress across sessions, recover state after context loss, coordinate multiple agents on the same project, audit project documentation health, or stop forgetting what was done last session. Triggers include: '/doc-harness init' and '/doc-harness check' (explicit slash commands); requests like 'help me set up this project', 'I keep losing track', 'my agent forgets between sessions', 'organize my project docs', 'audit this project', 'check the documentation', 'what did we do last time'; multi-week projects (theses, research, analyses, software modules) that span many sessions; cross-project coordination (inbox/outbox for file-based messages between projects)."
     4	argument-hint: "init [project-name] [description] | check | sync [--auto] | flush [--auto] | recall [query]"
     5	allowed-tools: Read, Write, Edit, Bash, Glob, Grep
     6	---
     7	
     8	# Doc Harness — Document-Based Project Control
     9	
    10	Doc Harness is a documentation system that enables any AI agent or human collaborator to understand and resume project work purely from reading files — no external memory needed.
    11	
    12	It creates and maintains **five documents** per project:
    13	- **CLAUDE.md** — Project entry point (overview, recovery chain, iron rules, operational rules)
    14	- **CURRENT_STATUS.md** — Active state (tire tracks / car body / headlights / driving manual)
    15	- **FILE_INDEX.md** — File catalog organized by category
    16	- **WORKLOG.md** — Permanent work history (append-only)
    17	- **DOC_HARNESS_SPEC.md** — Complete specification (reference document)
    18	
    19	Two **optional** documents may be added when a project accumulates such content (see spec.md Chapter 13):
    20	- **PARKING_LOT.md** — Deferred items with preconditions for revival


</details>

    10	Doc Harness 是一套文档管理系统，使任何 AI Agent 或人类协作者能够仅通过阅读文件来理解和恢复项目工作状态——无需任何外部记忆系统。

    16	- **WORKLOG.md** — 永久工作历史（只增不改）

     4	---
     5	
     6	# Doc Harness — Document-Based Project Control
     7	
     8	Doc Harness creates and maintains five status documents per project that enable any agent or human to understand and resume project work purely from reading files — no external memory needed.
     9	
    10	**Core principle**: "Write It Down or Lose It" — all information in context is temporary. If it is not written to a file and registered in FILE_INDEX, it will be lost.
    11	
    12	---
    13	
    14	## The Five Documents
    15	
    16	| Document | Role | Answers |
    17	|----------|------|---------|
    18	| **CLAUDE.md** | Project entry point | "What is this project? What are the rules? Where do I start?" |
    19	| **CURRENT_STATUS.md** | Active state | "What just happened? What's happening now? What's next?" |
    20	| **FILE_INDEX.md** | File catalog | "What files exist, what are they, and where are they?" |
    21	| **WORKLOG.md** | Permanent history | "What exactly happened in phase 2, three weeks ago?" |
    22	| **DOC_HARNESS_SPEC.md** | Complete reference | Full specification for unusual situations |
    23	
    24	**Metaphor**: A project in motion is like a **moving car**.
    25	- **Tire Tracks** (Recent Completed) — the road behind
    26	- **Car Body** (Current Work) — where you are right now
    27	- **Headlights** (Next Steps) — where you're going
    28	- **Driving Manual** (Working Principles) — rules for this road
    29	
    30	---
    31	
    32	## Natural-Language Commands
    33	
    34	Kimi has no slash commands. Use the table below to map user requests to the correct procedure.
    35	
    36	| User says | Procedure | See |
    37	|-----------|-----------|-----|
    38	| "Set up doc-harness" / "init project docs" / "create status documentation" | **Init** — create the five documents for a new or existing project | [references/init.md](references/init.md) |
    39	| "Check documentation health" / "audit project docs" / "run a health check" | **Check** — audit file health and reflect on principles | [references/check.md](references/check.md) |
    40	| "Sync project state" / "update status docs" / "catch up documentation" | **Sync** — repair drift, refresh dates, register missing files | [references/sync.md](references/sync.md) |
    41	| "Save everything" / "flush context" / "prepare for compact" / "ensure nothing is lost" | **Flush** — emergency save: extract all important context into documents | [references/flush.md](references/flush.md) |
    42	| "Recall" / "remember" / "find in docs" / "search project docs" / "where did we discuss" / "why did we decide" / "what is the current plan" | **Recall** — retrieve information from registered documents along the Doc Harness hierarchy | [references/recall.md](references/recall.md) |
    43	
    44	---
    45	
    46	## Daily Workflow
    47	
    48	### Session Start
    49	1. Read project's **CLAUDE.md** → understand overview, iron rules, recovery chain
    50	2. Read **CURRENT_STATUS.md** → tire tracks (history), car body (current state), headlights (next steps), driving manual (principles)
    51	3. If user is present → confirm whether next steps have changed
    52	4. If context was compressed → resume from car body per headlights
    53	
    54	### During Work
    55	- Complete a **meaningful step** → update CURRENT_STATUS car body
    56	- Create a new file → **do two things**: (1) register in FILE_INDEX (2) record in car body
    57	- Important analysis / decision / insight → **write to file immediately** and register
    58	- **Watch remaining context** (if runtime exposes it). When low (~<20%), update CURRENT_STATUS before the next tool call. If car body holds substantial unsaved work (≥3 steps / ≥50 lines / ≥100 lines), consider a phase transition now — compression is involuntary session end.
    59	
    60	### Session End
    61	1. Ensure car body reflects all work from this session
    62	2. Update headlights "next steps"
    63	3. Refresh CURRENT_STATUS "last updated" date
    64	4. Refresh CLAUDE.md "one-line status (as of date)"
    65	5. Check: all new files registered in FILE_INDEX?
    66	6. Check: any important information only in context? → Write it down!
    67	7. If phase transition occurred: WORKLOG under ~1000 lines? If over, archive per spec §5.5.
    68	
    69	---
    70	
    71	## Phase Transition (Five Steps)
    72	
    73	**Trigger**: Work goal fundamentally changes; user explicitly declares a new phase; project pauses (>3 days); car body exceeds ~200 lines.
    74	
    75	**Five steps (strict order)**:
    76	1. **Protect data**: Copy CURRENT_STATUS car body in full to WORKLOG top (after TOC). Add phase summary. → After this step, even if interrupted, no data is lost.
    77	2. Insert new summary (3-5 lines) at top of CURRENT_STATUS tire tracks.
    78	3. If tire tracks exceed 3 → remove the oldest (already in WORKLOG).
    79	4. Clear car body → fill in new phase goal. Review driving manual principles (promote to iron rule / keep / remove).
    80	5. Update CLAUDE.md "current phase" and "one-line status". Update WORKLOG TOC.
    81	
    82	**Interrupt safety**: Step 1 is protective. If compact occurs during Steps 2-5, data is safe. On next session start, run mid-transition detection (three-way coherence check: CLAUDE.md phase / WORKLOG TOC / CURRENT_STATUS tire tracks) and repair deterministically.
    83	
    84	---
    85	
    86	## Agent Behavior Rules
    87	
    88	### Iron Rules vs Driving Manual
    89	| Type | Location | Lifecycle |
    90	|------|----------|-----------|
    91	| **Iron rules** | CLAUDE.md | Permanent, phase-independent |
    92	| **Driving manual** | CURRENT_STATUS | Lives and dies with the phase |
    93	
    94	At phase transition, review each driving-manual principle: promote to iron rule (if ≥3 phases)? Keep? Remove?
    95	
    96	### Single Source of Truth
    97	| Fact Type | Sole Source |
    98	|-----------|------------|
    99	| Current state / progress | CURRENT_STATUS.md |
   100	| File catalog | FILE_INDEX.md |
   101	| Historical details | WORKLOG.md |
   102	| Project overview / rules | CLAUDE.md |
   103	
   104	### Anti-patterns
   105	- File created but not registered → register immediately
   106	- Information only in context → "Write It Down"
   107	- CURRENT_STATUS grows indefinitely → transfer to WORKLOG at phase transitions
   108	- WORKLOG grows past ~1000 lines untouched → archive per spec §5.5
   109	- Phase principles become permanent legacy → review at transition
   110	
   111	---
   112	
   113	## Optional Extensions
   114	
   115	- **PARKING_LOT.md** — Deferred items with preconditions for revival. Create only when needed.
   116	- **PHILOSOPHY.md** — Principles forged by project practice. Create only when insights generalize.
   117	- **inbox/outbox** — File-based cross-project messaging. Adopt only if project has dependencies.
   118	
   119	See [references/spec.md](references/spec.md) for full details.
   120	
   121	---
   122	
   123	## Reference Documents
   124	
   125	| File | When to read |
   126	|------|-------------|
   127	| [references/init.md](references/init.md) | User asks to set up / initialize doc-harness |
   128	| [references/check.md](references/check.md) | User asks to audit / check documentation health |
   129	| [references/sync.md](references/sync.md) | User asks to sync / update status docs |
   130	| [references/flush.md](references/flush.md) | User asks to save / flush context before compression |
   131	| [references/recall.md](references/recall.md) | User asks to recall / search / find information in project docs |
   132	| [references/spec.md](references/spec.md) | Unusual situation, edge case, or understanding design rationale |
   133	
   134	**Language note**: All documents are written in English with Chinese annotations where helpful. Kimi should respond in the user's language regardless of document language.


</details>

## Turn 9

### User

---
name: doc-harness
description: "Document-based project control that lets any AI agent or human resume work from files alone — no external memory needed. Use this skill whenever the user wants to structure a long-running project, track progress across sessions, recover state after context loss, coordinate multiple agents on the same project, audit project documentation health, or stop forgetting what was done last session. Triggers include: '/doc-harness init' and '/doc-harness check' (explicit slash commands); requests like 'help me set up this project', 'I keep losing track', 'my agent forgets between sessions', 'organize my project docs', 'audit this project', 'check the documentation', 'what did we do last time'; multi-week projects (theses, research, analyses, software modules) that span many sessions; cross-project coordination (inbox/outbox for file-based messages between projects)."
argument-hint: "init [project-name] [description] | check | sync [--auto] | flush [--auto] | recall [query]"
allowed-tools: Read, Write, Edit, Bash, Glob, Grep
---

# Doc Harness — Document-Based Project Control

Doc Harness is a documentation system that enables any AI agent or human collaborator to understand and resume project work purely from reading files — no external memory needed.

It creates and maintains **five documents** per project:
- **CLAUDE.md** — Project entry point (overview, recovery chain, iron rules, operational rules)
- **CURRENT_STATUS.md** — Active state (tire tracks / car body / headlights / driving manual)
- **FILE_INDEX.md** — File catalog organized by category
- **WORKLOG.md** — Permanent work history (append-only)
- **DOC_HARNESS_SPEC.md** — Complete specification (reference document)

Two **optional** documents may be added when a project accumulates such content (see spec.md Chapter 13):
- **PARKING_LOT.md** — Deferred items with preconditions for revival
- **PHILOSOPHY.md** — Principles forged by this project's practice

One **optional** mechanism may be adopted when a project coordinates with others (see spec.md Chapter 14):
- **Inter-project inbox/outbox** — self-contained file-based messaging protocol. `inbox/` and `outbox/` directories; YAML-frontmatter Markdown messages; lifecycle `unread → read → actioned`. Fully described inside doc-harness itself; no external spec needed.

## Commands

### `/doc-harness init [project-name] [description]`

Initialize Doc Harness for a new project. Creates all 5 files in the current directory.

**→ See [init.md](init.md) for full instructions and templates.**

### `/doc-harness check`

Audit the current project's documentation health and reflect on working principles.

**→ See [check.md](check.md) for full check procedures.**

### `/doc-harness sync [--auto]`

Synchronize status documents with reality. Repair drift, refresh stale fields, register missing files, and optionally trigger phase transition or WORKLOG archival.

- **`interactive`** (default): Ask before phase transitions, archival, or creating new principle documents.
- **`auto`**: Execute fixes without asking.

**→ See [sync.md](sync.md) for full sync procedures.**

### `/doc-harness flush [--auto]`

Emergency save before context compression. Includes everything `sync` does, plus mandatory extraction of important context information into documents.

- **`interactive`** (default): Ask before each significant extraction.
- **`auto`**: Use heuristics to classify and save context information without asking.

**→ See [flush.md](flush.md) for full flush procedures.**

### `/doc-harness recall [query]`

Retrieve information from the project's Doc Harness document hierarchy. Search systematically across registered documents and return structured, source-cited results.

**Query types**:
- **Status/Plan**: "What's the current plan for auth?" → searches CURRENT_STATUS + headlights
- **History/Decision**: "Why did we choose PostgreSQL?" → searches WORKLOG + tire tracks
- **File lookup**: "Find all docs about caching" → searches FILE_INDEX
- **Synthesis**: "All discussions about authentication" → comprehensive search across all layers

**→ See [recall.md](recall.md) for the layered search protocol and output format.**

### `/doc-harness` (no arguments)

Inspect the current directory and suggest the right next step:
- **All 4 core files present** (CLAUDE.md, CURRENT_STATUS.md, FILE_INDEX.md, WORKLOG.md) → suggest `/doc-harness check`.
- **No Doc Harness files at all** → suggest `/doc-harness init` (clean init or mid-project adoption per `init.md` Step 2).
- **Partial state** (some files present, others missing or malformed) → suggest `/doc-harness init` in **mid-project adoption mode** (see `init.md` Step 2 branch (b)/(c)); do NOT suggest `check` on a broken installation.

Then show this help summary.

## Core Principle: "Write It Down or Lose It"

Information in context will eventually be completely lost. Important information must be **written to a file** and **registered in FILE_INDEX**. Not written = lost. Not registered = undiscoverable = effectively lost.

**Context-aware corollary**: if your runtime exposes a context-window usage metric (percentage or token count), treat **low remaining context** (~<20%) as an immediate trigger to flush CURRENT_STATUS before the next tool call, and consider a phase transition if the car body holds substantial unsaved work (see `spec.md` §11.2 bullet 4 for the concrete threshold). Compression is involuntary session end — preemptive writes are the only defense.

## Reference Documents

- [init.md](init.md) — Read when executing `/doc-harness init`. Covers clean init, mid-project adoption, partial-state repair, and optional inter-project inbox/outbox setup.
- [check.md](check.md) — Read when executing `/doc-harness check`. Audit procedures for file health, recovery-chain soundness, mid-transition detection, and inbox status.
- [sync.md](sync.md) — Read when executing `/doc-harness sync`. Drift repair, date refresh, file registration, phase-transition and archival triggers.
- [flush.md](flush.md) — Read when executing `/doc-harness flush`. Emergency save with systematic context-to-document extraction.
- [recall.md](recall.md) — Read when executing `/doc-harness recall`. Layered search protocol for retrieving information from registered documents.
- [operational_rules.md](operational_rules.md) — The operational rules embedded verbatim into every project's CLAUDE.md at `init` time. Carries the `<!-- doc-harness-ops-version -->` version tag so the check command can detect stale embeddings.
- [spec.md](spec.md) — Complete Doc Harness specification (14 chapters + 5 appendices). Authoritative — all other files derive from it. Has a Table of Contents at the top for navigation without full-read.

#### Tool Call: Shell (`# Phase A: Sync scan # Check unregistered files $allFiles =…`)
<!-- call_id: tool_UU0Myd3qcG1tF0x04Pjx1Yqv -->
```json
{
  "command": "# Phase A: Sync scan\n# Check unregistered files\n$allFiles = Get-ChildItem -File -Recurse | Where-Object { \n    $_.FullName -notmatch '\\.git' -and \n    $_.FullName -notmatch 'node_modules' -and \n    $_.FullName -notmatch '_archive' \n} | Select-Object -ExpandProperty FullName | ForEach-Object { $_ -replace [regex]::Escape((Get-Location).Path + '\\'), '' } | Sort-Object\n\n$indexed = Select-String -Path \"FILE_INDEX.md\" -Pattern '\\`([^\\`]+)\\`' | ForEach-Object { \n    $m = $_ -match '\\`([^\\`]+)\\`'\n    if ($m) { $matches[1] }\n} | Sort-Object -Unique\n\n$unregistered = $allFiles | Where-Object { $_ -notin $indexed -and $_ -ne 'FILE_INDEX.md' }\nif ($unregistered.Count -eq 0) { \"No unregistered files\" } else { \"Unregistered: \" + ($unregistered -join ', ') }\n\n# Check dates\n\"\"\n\"CLAUDE.md date: \" + (Select-String -Path \"CLAUDE.md\" -Pattern \"Last updated\" | Select-Object -First 1)\n\"CURRENT_STATUS date: \" + (Select-String -Path \"CURRENT_STATUS.md\" -Pattern \"Last updated\" | Select-Object -First 1)\n\"FILE_INDEX date: \" + (Select-String -Path \"FILE_INDEX.md\" -Pattern \"Last updated\" | Select-Object -First 1)\n\n# Check car body length\n$carBodyStart = (Select-String -Path \"CURRENT_STATUS.md\" -Pattern \"## 当前工作|## Current Work\" | Select-Object -First 1).LineNumber\n$nextSection = (Select-String -Path \"CURRENT_STATUS.md\" -Pattern \"## \" | Where-Object { $_.LineNumber -gt $carBodyStart } | Select-Object -First 1).LineNumber\n$carBodyLines = $nextSection - $carBodyStart - 1\n\"Car body lines: $carBodyLines\"\n\n# Check WORKLOG length\n$worklogLines = (Get-Content \"WORKLOG.md\").Count\n\"WORKLOG lines: $worklogLines\""
}
```

    44	#### v1.5.0 design — sync + flush commands (2026-04-22)
    45	
    46	User requested two new commands to fill the gap between `check` (read-only diagnosis) and `init` (creation).
    47	
    48	- **`/doc-harness sync`** — Status synchronization. Repairs drift (unregistered files, stale dates), optionally triggers phase transition or WORKLOG archival. Two modes: `auto` (default, no asking) and `interactive` (asks before major changes). Distinct from `check`: sync modifies files; check only reports.
    49	- **`/doc-harness flush`** — Emergency context save. Includes everything sync does, PLUS mandatory extraction of important context information into documents before compression. Core guarantee: after flush, a new agent reading Recovery Chain recovers state as if context was never compressed. Two modes: `auto` (heuristic classification) and `interactive` (asks per item).

   154	
   155	## Current Working Principles (Driving Manual)
   156	
   157	*(Reviewed at phase transition per §6.2.2. Phase 3 principles that duplicated iron rules — bilingual sync, test before release, deployment sync — were removed since iron rules cover them permanently. Principles that responded to now-resolved constraints — inbox/outbox opt-in rule, portfolio-purge reminder — were removed since the spec now codifies those positions structurally. New principles specific to maintenance mode added below.)*
   158	
   159	- **Don't iterate without real user signal.** The v1.4 release extracted most of the latent issues a team of review agents could find through simulation. Further iteration from simulation alone has sharply diminishing returns; next changes should be driven by observed user problems, not hypothetical ones.
   160	- **v1.5 triggers are concrete**: ≥3 distinct real-world issues accumulated from field use, OR a breaking change in Claude Code's plugin system (e.g., marketplace.json schema change), OR a merge/comment on the awesome-claude-code submission that surfaces a needed change. Anything less, stay idle.
   161	- **If a release is triggered, re-run the 6-review pattern.** Don't skip review cycles because the change feels small. The v1.4 process found issues in cycles 5 and 6 that earlier cycles missed structurally, not accidentally.
   162	- **Define by what IS, not by what isn't.** (Carried over — applicable whenever new spec text is written. If no spec work, this principle is dormant but cheap to keep.)

```json
{
  "command": "# Recalculate car body lines properly\n$content = Get-Content \"CURRENT_STATUS.md\"\n$start = -1\n$end = -1\nfor ($i = 0; $i -lt $content.Count; $i++) {\n    if ($content[$i] -match \"^## Current Work|^## 当前工作\") { $start = $i }\n    if ($start -ne -1 -and $i -gt $start -and $content[$i] -match \"^---\") { $end = $i; break }\n}\nif ($end -eq -1) { $end = $content.Count }\n\"Car body: lines $start to $end = $($end - $start - 1) lines\""
}
```
